<p>The <b>Waffen-SS</b> (<small>German pronunciation:</small> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_German" title="Help:IPA for German">[ˈvafən.ɛs.ɛs]</a></span>, Armed SS) was the armed wing of the <a href="/wiki/Nazi_Party" title="Nazi Party">Nazi Party</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Schutzstaffel" title="Schutzstaffel">SS</a> organisation. Its formations included men from <a href="/wiki/Nazi_Germany" title="Nazi Germany">Nazi Germany</a>, along with volunteers and conscripts from both occupied and un-occupied lands.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEStein1984xxiv.2C_xxv.2C_150.2C_153_2-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEStein1984xxiv.2C_xxv.2C_150.2C_153-2">[2]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Waffen-SS grew from three <a href="/wiki/Regiment" title="Regiment">regiments</a> to over 38 <a href="/wiki/Division_(military)" title="Division (military)">divisions</a> during <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>, and served alongside the <i><a href="/wiki/German_Army_(Wehrmacht)" title="German Army (Wehrmacht)">Heer</a></i> (regular army), <i><a href="/wiki/Ordnungspolizei" title="Ordnungspolizei">Ordnungspolizei</a></i> (uniformed police) and other security units. Prior to the war, it was under the control of the <i><a href="/wiki/SS_F%C3%BChrungshauptamt" title="SS Führungshauptamt">SS Führungshauptamt</a></i> (SS operational command office) beneath <i><a href="/wiki/Reichsf%C3%BChrer-SS" title="Reichsführer-SS">Reichsführer-SS</a></i> <a href="/wiki/Heinrich_Himmler" title="Heinrich Himmler">Heinrich Himmler</a>. With the start of World War II, tactical control was exercised by the <a href="/wiki/Oberkommando_der_Wehrmacht" title="Oberkommando der Wehrmacht">High Command of the Armed Forces</a> (OKW),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEStein198423_3-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEStein198423-3">[3]</a></sup> with some units being subordinated to <a href="/wiki/Reichsf%C3%BChrer-SS#Kommandostab_Reichsf.C3.BChrer-SS" title="Reichsführer-SS"><i>Kommandostab Reichsführer-SS</i></a> (Command Staff Reichsführer-SS) directly under Himmler's control.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup></p>
<p>Initially, in keeping with the <a href="/wiki/Racial_policy_of_Nazi_Germany" title="Racial policy of Nazi Germany">racial policy of Nazi Germany</a>, membership was only open to people of Germanic origin (so-called <a href="/wiki/Aryan_race#Nazism" title="Aryan race">Aryan ancestry</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEStackelberg2002116_5-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEStackelberg2002116-5">[5]</a></sup> The rules were partially relaxed in 1940,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELangerRudowski2008263_6-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELangerRudowski2008263-6">[6]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKr.C3.B3l2006452.2C_545_7-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKr.C3.B3l2006452.2C_545-7">[7]</a></sup> and later the formation of units composed largely or solely of <a href="/wiki/Waffen-SS_foreign_volunteers_and_conscripts" title="Waffen-SS foreign volunteers and conscripts">foreign volunteers and conscripts</a> was authorised. These SS units were made up of men mainly from among the nationals of <a href="/wiki/Nazi_Germany" title="Nazi Germany">Nazi-occupied</a> Europe.</p>
<p>At the post-war <a href="/wiki/Nuremberg_trials" title="Nuremberg trials">Nuremberg trials</a> the Waffen-SS was judged to be a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Criminal_organisation" title="Criminal organisation">criminal organisation</a> due to its connection to the Nazi Party and involvement in numerous <a href="/wiki/War_crime" title="War crime">war crimes</a> and <a href="/wiki/Crimes_against_humanity" title="Crimes against humanity">crimes against humanity</a>. Former Waffen-SS members were denied many of the rights afforded to the military veterans. An exception was made for Waffen-SS conscripts, who were exempted because they were not volunteers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-laar2_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-laar2-9">[9]</a></sup> About a third of the total membership were conscripts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Origins_.281929.E2.80.9339.29">Origins (1929–39)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Waffen-SS&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Origins (1929–39)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_Bild_119-01-03,_Berlin,_Parade_zum_dritten_Jahrestag_LSSHA_crop.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="526" data-file-width="657" height="176" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Bundesarchiv_Bild_119-01-03%2C_Berlin%2C_Parade_zum_dritten_Jahrestag_LSSHA_crop.jpg/220px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_119-01-03%2C_Berlin%2C_Parade_zum_dritten_Jahrestag_LSSHA_crop.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Bundesarchiv_Bild_119-01-03%2C_Berlin%2C_Parade_zum_dritten_Jahrestag_LSSHA_crop.jpg/330px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_119-01-03%2C_Berlin%2C_Parade_zum_dritten_Jahrestag_LSSHA_crop.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Bundesarchiv_Bild_119-01-03%2C_Berlin%2C_Parade_zum_dritten_Jahrestag_LSSHA_crop.jpg/440px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_119-01-03%2C_Berlin%2C_Parade_zum_dritten_Jahrestag_LSSHA_crop.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_Bild_119-01-03,_Berlin,_Parade_zum_dritten_Jahrestag_LSSHA_crop.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Parade for the third anniversary of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1st_SS_Division_Leibstandarte_Adolf_Hitler" title="1st SS Division Leibstandarte Adolf Hitler">LSSAH</a> on the barracks' grounds. <a href="/wiki/Sepp_Dietrich" title="Sepp Dietrich">Sepp Dietrich</a> is at the lectern. May 1935</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The origins of the Waffen-SS can be traced back to the selection of a group of 120 SS men in March 1933 by <a href="/wiki/Sepp_Dietrich" title="Sepp Dietrich">Sepp Dietrich</a> to form the <i>Sonderkommando</i> Berlin.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFlaherty2004144_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFlaherty2004144-11">[11]</a></sup> By November 1933 the formation had 800 men, and at a commemorative ceremony in Munich for the tenth anniversary of the failed <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Munich_Putsch" title="Munich Putsch">Munich Putsch</a> the regiment swore allegiance to <a href="/wiki/Adolf_Hitler" title="Adolf Hitler">Adolf Hitler</a>. The oaths pledged were "Pledging loyalty to him alone" and "Obedience unto death".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFlaherty2004144_11-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFlaherty2004144-11">[11]</a></sup> The formation was given the title <i>Leibstandarte</i> (Bodyguard Regiment) <i>Adolf Hitler</i> (LAH).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECookBender199417.2C_19_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECookBender199417.2C_19-12">[12]</a></sup> On 13 April 1934, by order of Himmler, the regiment became known as the <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1st_SS_Division_Leibstandarte_Adolf_Hitler" title="1st SS Division Leibstandarte Adolf Hitler">Leibstandarte SS Adolf Hitler</a></i> (LSSAH).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECookBender199417.2C_19_12-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECookBender199417.2C_19-12">[12]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <i>Leibstandarte</i> demonstrated their loyalty to Hitler in 1934 during the <a href="/wiki/Night_of_the_Long_Knives" title="Night of the Long Knives">Night of the Long Knives</a>, when the Nazi regime carried out a series of political killings and the purge of the <i><a href="/wiki/Sturmabteilung" title="Sturmabteilung">Sturmabteilung</a></i> (SA).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFlaherty2004144_11-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFlaherty2004144-11">[11]</a></sup> Led by one of Hitler's oldest comrades, <a href="/wiki/Ernst_R%C3%B6hm" title="Ernst Röhm">Ernst Röhm</a>, the SA was seen as a threat by Hitler to his newly gained political power. Hitler also wanted to conciliate leaders of the <a href="/wiki/Reichswehr" title="Reichswehr">Reichswehr</a> and conservatives of the country, people whose support Hitler needed to solidify his position. When Hitler decided to act against the SA, the SS was put in charge of eliminating Röhm and the other high-ranking SA officers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKershaw2008306.E2.80.93313_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKershaw2008306.E2.80.93313-13">[13]</a></sup> The Night of the Long Knives occurred from between 30 June and 2 July 1934 and saw the killing of approximately 82 SA men, including almost its entire leadership, effectively ending the power of the SA. This action was largely carried out by the <i>Leibstandarte</i> and other SS personnel.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFlaherty2004144_11-3"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFlaherty2004144-11">[11]</a></sup></p>
<p>In September 1934, Hitler authorized the formation of the military wing of the <a href="/wiki/Nazi_Party" title="Nazi Party">Nazi Party</a> and approved the formation of the <i><a href="/wiki/SS-Verf%C3%BCgungstruppe" title="SS-Verfügungstruppe">SS-Verfügungstruppe</a></i> (SS-VT), a special service troop under Hitler's overall command.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFlaherty2004144_11-4"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFlaherty2004144-11">[11]</a></sup> The SS-VT had to depend on the <a href="/wiki/German_Army_(Wehrmacht)" title="German Army (Wehrmacht)">German Army</a> for its supply of weapons and military training, and they had control of the recruiting system through local draft boards responsible for assigning conscripts to the different branches of the Wehrmacht to meet quotas set by the <a href="/wiki/Oberkommando_der_Wehrmacht" title="Oberkommando der Wehrmacht">German High Command</a> (Oberkommando der Wehrmacht or OKW in German). The SS was given the lowest priority for recruits.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFlaherty2004145_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFlaherty2004145-14">[14]</a></sup></p>
<p>Even with the difficulties presented by the quota system, <a href="/wiki/Heinrich_Himmler" title="Heinrich Himmler">Heinrich Himmler</a> formed two new SS regiments, the <i>SS Germania</i> and <i>SS Deutschland</i>, which together with the <i>Leibstandarte</i> and a communications unit made up the SS-VT.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFlaherty2004145_14-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFlaherty2004145-14">[14]</a></sup> At the same time Himmler established the <a href="/wiki/SS-Junkerschule_Bad_T%C3%B6lz" title="SS-Junkerschule Bad Tölz">SS-Junkerschule Bad Tölz</a> and <a href="/wiki/Braunschweig" title="Braunschweig">SS-Junkerschule Braunschweig</a> for military training of SS officers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFlaherty2004145_14-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFlaherty2004145-14">[14]</a></sup> Both schools used regular army training methods and mainly used former army officers as instructors.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFlaherty2004145_14-3"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFlaherty2004145-14">[14]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_Bild_146-1972-061-38,_Berlin,_vor_Krolloper,_Hitler_mit_Leibstandarte.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="800" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Bundesarchiv_Bild_146-1972-061-38%2C_Berlin%2C_vor_Krolloper%2C_Hitler_mit_Leibstandarte.jpg/220px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_146-1972-061-38%2C_Berlin%2C_vor_Krolloper%2C_Hitler_mit_Leibstandarte.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Bundesarchiv_Bild_146-1972-061-38%2C_Berlin%2C_vor_Krolloper%2C_Hitler_mit_Leibstandarte.jpg/330px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_146-1972-061-38%2C_Berlin%2C_vor_Krolloper%2C_Hitler_mit_Leibstandarte.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Bundesarchiv_Bild_146-1972-061-38%2C_Berlin%2C_vor_Krolloper%2C_Hitler_mit_Leibstandarte.jpg/440px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_146-1972-061-38%2C_Berlin%2C_vor_Krolloper%2C_Hitler_mit_Leibstandarte.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_Bild_146-1972-061-38,_Berlin,_vor_Krolloper,_Hitler_mit_Leibstandarte.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <i>Leibstandarte SS Adolf Hitler</i> parades in Berlin, 1938</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Himmler initially in 1934 set stringent requirements for recruits. They were to be German nationals who could prove their Aryan ancestry back to 1800, unmarried, and without a criminal record.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWeale2012202_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWeale2012202-15">[15]</a></sup> A four-year commitment was required for the SS-VT and LSSAH. Recruits had to be between the ages of 17 and 23, at least 1.74 metres (5 ft 9 in) tall (1.78 metres (5 ft 10 in) for the LSSAH). Concentration camp guards had to make a one-year commitment, be between the ages of 16 and 23, and at least 1.72 metres (5 ft 8 in) tall. All recruits were required to have no dental fillings, 20/20 eyesight and provide a medical certificate.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWeale2012201.E2.80.93204_16-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWeale2012201.E2.80.93204-16">[16]</a></sup> By 1938 the height restrictions were relaxed, up to six dental fillings were permitted, and eyeglasses for astigmatism and mild vision correction were allowed. Once the war commenced, the physical requirements were no longer strictly enforced, and essentially any recruit who could pass a basic medical exam was considered for service.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWeale2010204_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWeale2010204-17">[17]</a></sup> Members of the SS could be of any religion except Judaism (Jewish), but atheists were not allowed according to Himmler in 1937.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELongerich2012220_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELongerich2012220-18">[18]</a></sup></p>
<p>The officers of the SS were almost all of lower middle-class or working-class origin, who would have not been considered for commissioning in the old German Army. In the SS they could take part in the <i>gentlemanly rituals</i> of the mess. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fritz_Langanke" title="Fritz Langanke">Fritz Langanke</a> was the son of a miner. Major Heinrich Wulf, commander of the Das Reich reconnaissance battalion, was the son of a North German worker who died as a conscript in Flanders in 1917. Major Gunther-Eberhardt Wisliceny the commander of the Deutschland Panzergrenadier regiment was described as looking like a tall, stiff Prussian Junker, but had been a miner in Silesia for three years. Major Otto Weidinger was the son of a post office worker, and he was rejected by both the army and the police before acceptance into the SS.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHastings20137.E2.80.938_19-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHastings20137.E2.80.938-19">[19]</a></sup> But some were from the old elite, like Otto Pohl (commander of a tank unit); his father, an officer in the navy, joined Hitler in the 1920s and became a SS General.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHastings201311_20-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHastings201311-20">[20]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1936, Himmler selected former Lieutenant General <a href="/wiki/Paul_Hausser" title="Paul Hausser">Paul Hausser</a> to be Inspector of the SS-VT with the rank of <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Brigadefuhrer" title="Brigadefuhrer">Brigadefuhrer</a></i>. Hausser worked to transform the SS-VT into a credible military force that was a match for the regular army.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFlaherty2004146_21-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFlaherty2004146-21">[21]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWindrowBurn19927.E2.80.938_22-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWindrowBurn19927.E2.80.938-22">[22]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 17 August 1938, Hitler declared that the SS-VT would have a role in domestic as well as foreign affairs, which transformed this growing armed force into the rival that the army had feared.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFlaherty2004147_23-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFlaherty2004147-23">[23]</a></sup> He decreed that service in the SS-VT qualified to fulfill military service obligations, although service in the <i><a href="/wiki/SS-Totenkopfverb%C3%A4nde" title="SS-Totenkopfverbände">SS-Totenkopfverbände</a></i> or SS-TV would not. Some units of the SS-TV would, in the case of war, be used as reserves for the SS-VT, which did not have its own reserves.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFlaherty2004148_24-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFlaherty2004148-24">[24]</a></sup> For all its training, the SS-VT was untested in combat. In 1938, a battalion of the <i>Leibstandarte</i> was chosen to accompany the army troops in occupying <a href="/wiki/Austria" title="Austria">Austria</a> during the <i><a href="/wiki/Anschluss" title="Anschluss">Anschluss</a></i>, and the three regiments of the SS-VT participated in the occupation of the <a href="/wiki/Sudetenland" title="Sudetenland">Sudetenland</a> that October. In both actions no resistance was met.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWindrowBurn19927.E2.80.938_22-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWindrowBurn19927.E2.80.938-22">[22]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFlaherty2004148_24-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFlaherty2004148-24">[24]</a></sup></p>
<p>Recruiting of ethnic Germans from other countries began in April 1940, and units consisting of non-Germanic recruits were formed beginning in 1942.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELongerich2012500.2C_674_25-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELongerich2012500.2C_674-25">[25]</a></sup> Non-Germanic units were not considered to be part of the SS, which still maintained its racial criteria, but rather were considered to be foreign nationals serving under the command of the SS.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELongerich2012769_26-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELongerich2012769-26">[26]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="World_War_II">World War II</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Waffen-SS&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: World War II">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1939">1939</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Waffen-SS&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: 1939">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Invasion_of_Poland">Invasion of Poland</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Waffen-SS&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Invasion of Poland">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_Bild_146-1968-034-19A,_Exekution_von_polnischen_Geiseln.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="475" data-file-width="795" height="131" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Bundesarchiv_Bild_146-1968-034-19A%2C_Exekution_von_polnischen_Geiseln.jpg/220px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_146-1968-034-19A%2C_Exekution_von_polnischen_Geiseln.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Bundesarchiv_Bild_146-1968-034-19A%2C_Exekution_von_polnischen_Geiseln.jpg/330px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_146-1968-034-19A%2C_Exekution_von_polnischen_Geiseln.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Bundesarchiv_Bild_146-1968-034-19A%2C_Exekution_von_polnischen_Geiseln.jpg/440px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_146-1968-034-19A%2C_Exekution_von_polnischen_Geiseln.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_Bild_146-1968-034-19A,_Exekution_von_polnischen_Geiseln.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
SS <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Einsatzgruppe" title="Einsatzgruppe">Einsatzgruppe</a></i> members murdering Polish civilians in <a href="/wiki/K%C3%B3rnik" title="Kórnik">Kórnik</a> shortly after the outbreak of World War II in Europe</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Himmler's military formations at the outbreak of the war comprised several subgroups which would become the basis of the Waffen-SS.</p>
<ul>
<li>The <i>Leibstandarte SS Adolf Hitler</i> (LSSAH), under then <i>Obergruppenführer</i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[a]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Sepp_Dietrich" title="Sepp Dietrich">Josef "Sepp" Dietrich</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEStein19844.E2.80.938.2C_27_28-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEStein19844.E2.80.938.2C_27-28">[27]</a></sup></li>
<li>The Inspectorate of <i>Verfügungstruppe</i> (SS-VT), under <i>Gruppenführer</i> <a href="/wiki/Paul_Hausser" title="Paul Hausser">Paul Hausser</a>, which commanded the <i>Deutschland</i>, <i>Germania</i> and <i>Der Führer</i> regiments. The latter was recruited in Austria after the <a href="/wiki/Anschluss" title="Anschluss">Anschluss</a> and was not yet combat-ready.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFlaherty2004149_29-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFlaherty2004149-29">[28]</a></sup></li>
<li>The Inspectorate of Concentration Camps, under <i>Gruppenführer</i> <a href="/wiki/Theodor_Eicke" title="Theodor Eicke">Theodor Eicke</a>, which fielded four infantry and one cavalry <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/3rd_SS_Division_Totenkopf" title="3rd SS Division Totenkopf">Death's-Head <i>Standarten</i></a>, comprising camp guards of the <i>SS-Totenkopfverbände</i> (SS-TV). These troops wore the SS-TV skull and crossbones rather than the SS-VT "SS" runes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEStein198427.2C_28.2C_33.2C_34_30-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEStein198427.2C_28.2C_33.2C_34-30">[29]</a></sup></li>
<li>Police units of <i>Obergruppenführer und General der Polizei</i> <a href="/wiki/Kurt_Daluege" title="Kurt Daluege">Kurt Daluege</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Ordnungspolizei" title="Ordnungspolizei">Ordnungspolizei</a></i>, which reported to Himmler in his capacity as Chief of German Police. These troops used police <a href="/wiki/Ranks_and_insignia_of_the_Ordnungspolizei" title="Ranks and insignia of the Ordnungspolizei">ranks and insignia</a> rather than those of the SS.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEStein1984xxii.2C_35.2C_36_31-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEStein1984xxii.2C_35.2C_36-31">[30]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<p>In August 1939, Hitler placed the <i>Leibstandarte</i> and the SS-VT under the operational control of the Army High Command (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/OKH" title="OKH">OKH</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFlaherty2004149_29-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFlaherty2004149-29">[28]</a></sup> Himmler retained command of the <i>Totenkopfstandarten,</i> for employment behind the advancing combat units in what were euphemistically called "special tasks of a police nature".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEStein198424_32-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEStein198424-32">[31]</a></sup></p>
<p>In spite of the swift military victory over <a href="/wiki/Invasion_of_Poland" title="Invasion of Poland">Poland</a> in September 1939, the regular army felt that the performance of the SS-VT left much to be desired; its units took unnecessary risks and had a higher casualty rate than the army.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFlaherty2004149_29-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFlaherty2004149-29">[28]</a></sup> They also stated that the SS-VT was poorly trained and its officers unsuitable for combat command. As an example, OKW noted that the <i>Leibstandarte</i> had to be rescued by an army regiment after becoming surrounded at <a href="/wiki/Pabianice" title="Pabianice">Pabianice</a> by the Poles.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFlaherty2004149_29-3"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFlaherty2004149-29">[28]</a></sup> In its defence, the SS insisted that it had been hampered by having to fight piecemeal instead of as one formation, and was improperly equipped by the army to carry out its objectives.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFlaherty2004149_29-4"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFlaherty2004149-29">[28]</a></sup> Himmler insisted that the SS-VT should be allowed to fight in its own formations under its own commanders, while the OKW tried to have the SS-VT disbanded altogether.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFlaherty2004149_29-5"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFlaherty2004149-29">[28]</a></sup> Hitler was unwilling to upset either the army or Himmler, and chose a third path. He ordered that the SS-VT form its own divisions but that the divisions would be under army command.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFlaherty2004149_29-6"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFlaherty2004149-29">[28]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Adolf_Hitler" title="Adolf Hitler">Adolf Hitler</a> resisted integrating the Waffen-SS into the army, as it was intended to remain the armed wing of the Party and to become an elite police force once the war was won.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEReitlinger198984_33-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEReitlinger198984-33">[32]</a></sup></p>
<p>During the invasion, war crimes were committed against the Polish people. The <i>Leibstandarte</i> became notorious for torching villages without military justification.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEButler200145_34-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEButler200145-34">[33]</a></sup> Members of the <i>Leibstandarte</i> also committed atrocities in numerous towns, including the murder of 50 Polish Jews in <a href="/wiki/B%C5%82onie" title="Błonie">Błonie</a> and the massacre of 200 civilians, including children, who were machine gunned in <a href="/wiki/Z%C5%82oczew" title="Złoczew">Złoczew</a>. Shootings also took place in <a href="/wiki/Boles%C5%82awiec" title="Bolesławiec">Bolesławiec</a>, <a href="/wiki/Torzeniec" title="Torzeniec">Torzeniec</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Goworowo" title="Goworowo">Goworowo</a>, <a href="/wiki/M%C5%82awa" title="Mława">Mława</a>, and <a href="/wiki/W%C5%82oc%C5%82awek" title="Włocławek">Włocławek</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERossino2003114.2C_159.E2.80.93161_35-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERossino2003114.2C_159.E2.80.93161-35">[34]</a></sup> Eicke's SS-TV field forces were not military. "Their military capabilities were employed instead in terrorizing the civilian population through acts that included hunting down straggling Polish soldiers, confiscating agricultural produce and livestock, and torturing and murdering large numbers of Polish political leaders, aristocrats, businessmen, priests, intellectuals, and Jews."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESydnor199037_36-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESydnor199037-36">[35]</a></sup> His <i>Totenkopfverbände</i> troops were called on to carry out "police and security measures" in the rear areas. What these measures involved is demonstrated by the record of <i>SS Totenkopf Standarte "Brandenburg"</i>. It arrived in <a href="/wiki/W%C5%82oc%C5%82awek" title="Włocławek">Włocławek</a> on 22 September 1939 and embarked on a four-day "Jewish action" that included the burning of synagogues and the execution en-masse of the leaders of the Jewish community. On 29 September the <i>Standarte</i> travelled to Bydgoszcz to conduct an "<a href="/wiki/Intelligenzaktion" title="Intelligenzaktion">intelligentsia action</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wardzy.C5.84ska2009_37-0"><a href="#cite_note-Wardzy.C5.84ska2009-37">[36]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="First_Divisions">First Divisions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Waffen-SS&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: First Divisions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>In October 1939, <i>Deutschland</i>, <i>Germania</i>, and <i>Der Führer</i> regiments were reorganized into the <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/SS-Verf%C3%BCgungs-Division" title="SS-Verfügungs-Division">SS-Verfügungs-Division</a></i>. The <i>Leibstandarte</i> remained independent and was increased in strength to a reinforced motorized regiment.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFlaherty2004149_29-7"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFlaherty2004149-29">[28]</a></sup> Hitler authorized the creation of two new divisions: the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/3rd_SS_Division_Totenkopf" title="3rd SS Division Totenkopf">SS <i>Totenkopf</i> Division</a>, formed from militarized <i>Standarten</i> of the <i><a href="/wiki/SS-Totenkopfverb%C3%A4nde" title="SS-Totenkopfverbände">SS-Totenkopfverbände</a></i>, and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/4th_SS_Polizei_Division" title="4th SS Polizei Division">Polizei Division</a>, formed from members of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Orpo" title="Orpo">national police force</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFlaherty2004149.E2.80.93150_38-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFlaherty2004149.E2.80.93150-38">[37]</a></sup> Almost overnight the force that the OKW had tried to disband had increased from 18,000 to over 100,000 men.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFlaherty2004150_39-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFlaherty2004150-39">[38]</a></sup> Hitler next authorized the creation in March 1940 of four Motorized Artillery battalions, one for each division and the <i>Leibstandarte</i>. The OKW was supposed to supply these new battalions with artillery, but was reluctant to hand over guns from its own arsenal. The weapons arrived only slowly, and by the time of the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_France" title="Battle of France">Battle of France</a> only the <i>Leibstandarte</i> battalion was up to strength.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFlaherty2004151_40-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFlaherty2004151-40">[39]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1940">1940</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Waffen-SS&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: 1940">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="France_and_the_Netherlands">France and the Netherlands</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Waffen-SS&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: France and the Netherlands">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The three SS divisions and the <i>Leibstandarte</i> spent the winter of 1939 and the spring of 1940 training and preparing for the coming war in the west. In May they moved to the front, and the <i>Leibstandarte</i> became part of the Army's <a href="/wiki/227th_Infantry_Division_(Wehrmacht)" title="227th Infantry Division (Wehrmacht)">227th Infantry Division</a>. The <i>Der Führer</i> Regiment was detached from the SS-VT Division and relocated near the Dutch border, with the remainder of the division behind the line in <a href="/wiki/M%C3%BCnster" title="Münster">Münster</a>, awaiting the order to invade the <a href="/wiki/Netherlands" title="Netherlands">Netherlands</a>. The SS <i>Totenkopf</i> and Polizei Divisions were held in reserve.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFlaherty2004152_41-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFlaherty2004152-41">[40]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 10 May the <i>Leibstandarte</i>, wearing Dutch uniforms, overcame Dutch border guards to spearhead the German advance into the Netherlands, and the <i>Der Führer</i> advanced towards <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Utrecht_(city)" title="Utrecht (city)">Utrecht</a>. The following day the rest of the SS-VT Division crossed into the Netherlands and headed towards <a href="/wiki/Rotterdam" title="Rotterdam">Rotterdam</a>, which they reached on 12 May.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFlaherty2004152_41-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFlaherty2004152-41">[40]</a></sup> After the surrender of Rotterdam, the <i>Leibstandarte</i> left for the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hague" title="Hague">Hague</a>, which they reached on 15 May, capturing 3,500 Dutch as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Prisoners_of_war" title="Prisoners of war">prisoners of war</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFlaherty2004154_42-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFlaherty2004154-42">[41]</a></sup></p>
<p>In France the SS <i>Totenkopf</i> was involved in the only Allied tank attack in the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_France" title="Battle of France">Battle of France</a>. On 21 May units of the <a href="/wiki/1st_Army_Tank_Brigade_(United_Kingdom)" title="1st Army Tank Brigade (United Kingdom)">1st Army Tank Brigade</a>, supported by the <a href="/wiki/50th_(Northumbrian)_Infantry_Division" title="50th (Northumbrian) Infantry Division">50th (Northumbrian) Infantry Division</a>, took part in the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Arras_(1940)" title="Battle of Arras (1940)">Battle of Arras</a>. The SS <i>Totenkopf</i> was overrun, finding their standard <a href="/wiki/Anti-tank_gun" title="Anti-tank gun">anti-tank gun</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/3.7_cm_PaK_36" title="3.7 cm PaK 36">3.7 cm PaK 36</a>, was no match for the British <a href="/wiki/Matilda_II" title="Matilda II">Matilda tank</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarman1980100_43-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarman1980100-43">[42]</a></sup></p>
<p>After the Dutch surrender, the <i>Leibstandarte</i> moved south to France on 24 May. Becoming part of the XIX Panzer Corps under the command of General <a href="/wiki/Heinz_Guderian" title="Heinz Guderian">Heinz Guderian</a>, they took up a position 15 miles south west of <a href="/wiki/Dunkirk" title="Dunkirk">Dunkirk</a> along the line of the Aa Canal, facing the Allied defensive line near Watten.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFlaherty2004154_42-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFlaherty2004154-42">[41]</a></sup> A patrol from the SS-VT Division crossed the canal at <a href="/wiki/Saint-Venant" title="Saint-Venant">Saint-Venant</a>, but was destroyed by British armor. A larger force from the SS-VT Division then crossed the canal and formed a bridgehead at Saint-Venant; 30 miles from Dunkirk.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFlaherty2004154_42-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFlaherty2004154-42">[41]</a></sup> That night the OKW ordered the advance to halt, with the <a href="/wiki/British_Expeditionary_Force_(World_War_II)" title="British Expeditionary Force (World War II)">British Expeditionary Force</a> trapped. The <i>Leibstandarte</i> paused for the night. However, on the following day, in defiance of Hitler's orders, Dietrich ordered his III Battalion to cross the canal and take the heights beyond, where <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">British</a> artillery observers were putting the regiment at risk. They assaulted the heights and drove the observers off. Instead of being censured for his act of defiance, Dietrich was awarded the <a href="/wiki/Knight%27s_Cross_of_the_Iron_Cross" title="Knight's Cross of the Iron Cross">Knight's Cross of the Iron Cross</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFlaherty2004143.2C_154_44-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFlaherty2004143.2C_154-44">[43]</a></sup> On that same day, British forces attacked Saint-Venant, forcing the SS-VT Division to retreat and relinquish ground.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFlaherty2004154_42-3"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFlaherty2004154-42">[41]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 26 May the German advance resumed. On 27 May the <i>Deutschland</i> regiment of the SS-VT Division reached the allied defensive line on the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Leie_River" title="Leie River">Leie River</a> at <a href="/wiki/Merville,_Nord" title="Merville, Nord">Merville</a>. They forced a bridgehead across the river and waited for the SS <i>Totenkopf</i> Division to arrive to cover their flank. What arrived first was a unit of British tanks, which penetrated their position. The SS-VT managed to hold on against the British tank force, which got to within 15 feet of commander <a href="/wiki/Felix_Steiner" title="Felix Steiner">Felix Steiner</a>'s position. Only the arrival of the <i>Totenkopf</i> <a href="/wiki/Panzerj%C3%A4ger" title="Panzerjäger">Panzerjäger</a> platoon saved the <i>Deutschland</i> from being destroyed and their bridgehead lost.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFlaherty2004155_45-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFlaherty2004155-45">[44]</a></sup></p>
<p>That same day, as the SS <i>Totenkopf</i> Division advanced near Merville, they encountered stubborn resistance from British Army units which slowed their advance.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFlaherty2004155_45-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFlaherty2004155-45">[44]</a></sup> The SS <i>Totenkopf</i> 4 Company, then committed the <a href="/wiki/Le_Paradis_massacre" title="Le Paradis massacre">Le Paradis massacre</a>, where 97 captured men of the 2nd Battalion, <a href="/wiki/Royal_Norfolk_Regiment" title="Royal Norfolk Regiment">Royal Norfolk Regiment</a> were machine gunned after surrendering, with survivors finished off with <a href="/wiki/Bayonet" title="Bayonet">bayonets</a>. Two men survived.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[45]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEJackson2001285.E2.80.93288_47-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEJackson2001285.E2.80.93288-47">[46]</a></sup></p>
<p>By 28 May the <i>Leibstandarte</i> had taken the village of <a href="/wiki/Wormhout" title="Wormhout">Wormhout</a>, only ten miles from Dunkirk.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFlaherty2004154_42-4"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFlaherty2004154-42">[41]</a></sup> After their surrender, soldiers from the 2nd Battalion, <a href="/wiki/Royal_Warwickshire_Regiment" title="Royal Warwickshire Regiment">Royal Warwickshire Regiment</a>, along with some other units (including <a href="/wiki/French_Army" title="French Army">French soldiers</a>) were taken to a barn in <i>La Plaine au Bois</i> near <a href="/wiki/Wormhout" title="Wormhout">Wormhout</a> and <a href="/wiki/Esquelbecq" title="Esquelbecq">Esquelbecq</a>. It was there that troops of the <i>Leibstandarte</i> 2nd Battalion committed the <a href="/wiki/Wormhoudt_massacre" title="Wormhoudt massacre">Wormhoudt massacre</a>, where 80 British and French prisoners of war were killed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEButler200181.E2.80.9383_48-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEButler200181.E2.80.9383-48">[47]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWeale2012251.E2.80.93253_49-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWeale2012251.E2.80.93253-49">[48]</a></sup></p>
<p>By 30 May the British were <a href="/wiki/Dunkirk_evacuation" title="Dunkirk evacuation">cornered at Dunkirk</a>, and the SS divisions continued the advance into France. The <i>Leibstandarte</i> reached <a href="/wiki/Saint-%C3%89tienne" title="Saint-Étienne">Saint-Étienne</a>, 250 miles south of Paris, and had advanced further into France than any other unit.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFlaherty2004143_50-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFlaherty2004143-50">[49]</a></sup> By the next day the fighting was all but over.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFlaherty2004156_51-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFlaherty2004156-51">[50]</a></sup> German forces arrived in Paris unopposed on 14 June and France formally surrendered on 25 June. Hitler expressed his pleasure with the performance of the <i>Leibstandarte</i> in the Netherlands and France, telling them, "Henceforth it will be an honour for you, who bear my name, to lead every German attack."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFlaherty2004143_50-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFlaherty2004143-50">[49]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="1940_expansion">1940 expansion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Waffen-SS&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: 1940 expansion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Waffen-SS_foreign_volunteers_and_conscripts" title="Waffen-SS foreign volunteers and conscripts">Waffen-SS foreign volunteers and conscripts</a></div>
<p>Himmler gained approval for the Waffen-SS to form its own high command, the <i>Kommandoamt der Waffen-SS</i> within the <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/SS-F%C3%BChrungshauptamt" title="SS-Führungshauptamt">SS-Führungshauptamt</a></i>, which was created in August 1940.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEStein1984102_52-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEStein1984102-52">[51]</a></sup> It received command of the SS-VT (the <i>Leibstandarte</i> and the <i>Verfügungs-Division</i>, renamed <i>Reich</i>) and the armed SS-TV regiments (the <i>Totenkopf-Division</i> together with several independent <i>Totenkopf-Standarten</i>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEStein19847.2C_103.E2.80.93106_53-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEStein19847.2C_103.E2.80.93106-53">[52]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1940 SS chief of staff <a href="/wiki/Gottlob_Berger" title="Gottlob Berger">Gottlob Berger</a> approached Himmler with a plan to recruit volunteers in the conquered territories from the ethnic German and Germanic populations. At first Hitler had doubts about recruiting foreigners, but he was persuaded by Himmler and Berger.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEStein1984150.2C_153_54-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEStein1984150.2C_153-54">[53]</a></sup> He gave approval for a new division to be formed from foreign nationals with German officers. By June 1940, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Danish_ethnic_group" title="Danish ethnic group">Danish</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Norwegian_people" title="Norwegian people">Norwegian</a> volunteers had formed the SS Regiment <i><a href="/wiki/11th_SS_Volunteer_Panzergrenadier_Division_Nordland" title="11th SS Volunteer Panzergrenadier Division Nordland">Nordland</a></i>, with <a href="/wiki/Dutch_people" title="Dutch people">Dutch</a> and <a href="/wiki/Flanders" title="Flanders">Flemish</a> volunteers forming the SS Regiment <i>Westland</i>. The two regiments, together with <i>Germania</i> (transferred from the <i>Reich</i> Division), formed the <a href="/wiki/5th_SS_Panzer_Division_Wiking" title="5th SS Panzer Division Wiking">SS Division <i>Wiking</i></a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFlaherty2004160.2C_161_55-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFlaherty2004160.2C_161-55">[54]</a></sup> A sufficient number of volunteers came forward requiring the SS to open a new training camp just for foreign volunteers at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sennheim" title="Sennheim">Sennheim</a> in <a href="/wiki/Alsace-Lorraine" title="Alsace-Lorraine">Alsace-Lorraine</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFlaherty2004160.2C_161_55-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFlaherty2004160.2C_161-55">[54]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Finnish_SS_volunteers_in_Gross_Born.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="255" data-file-width="400" height="140" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Finnish_SS_volunteers_in_Gross_Born.jpg/220px-Finnish_SS_volunteers_in_Gross_Born.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Finnish_SS_volunteers_in_Gross_Born.jpg/330px-Finnish_SS_volunteers_in_Gross_Born.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/4/4a/Finnish_SS_volunteers_in_Gross_Born.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>

</div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1941">1941</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Waffen-SS&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: 1941">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>At the beginning of the new year the <i>Polizei-Division</i> was brought under FHA administration, although it would not be formally merged into the Waffen-SS until 1942. At the same time the <i>Totenkopf-Standarten</i>, aside from the three constituting the TK-Division, lost their Death's Head designation and insignia and were reclassified <i>SS-Infanterie-</i> (or <i>Kavallerie-</i>) <i>Regimente</i>. The 11th Rgt. was transferred into the <i>Reich</i> Division to replace <i>Germania</i>; the remainder were grouped into three independent brigades and a battle group in Norway.</p>
<p>By the spring of 1941 the Waffen-SS consisted of the equivalent of six or seven divisions: the <i><a href="/wiki/2nd_SS_Panzer_Division_Das_Reich" title="2nd SS Panzer Division Das Reich">Reich</a></i>, <i>Totenkopf</i>, <i>Polizei</i>, and <i>Wiking</i> Divisions and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/6_SS" title="6 SS"><i>Kampfgruppe</i> (later Division) <i>Nord</i></a>, and the <i>Leibstandarte</i>, <a href="/wiki/1_SS_Infantry_Brigade" title="1 SS Infantry Brigade">1 SS Infantry</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2_SS_Infantry_Brigade" title="2 SS Infantry Brigade">2 SS Infantry</a>, and <a href="/wiki/SS_Cavalry_Brigade" title="SS Cavalry Brigade">SS Cavalry</a> Brigades.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Balkans">Balkans</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Waffen-SS&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Balkans">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_Bild_101I-158-0094-35,_Balkan,_PKW_der_Leibstandarte_Adolf_Hitler.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="544" data-file-width="800" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Bundesarchiv_Bild_101I-158-0094-35%2C_Balkan%2C_PKW_der_Leibstandarte_Adolf_Hitler.jpg/220px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_101I-158-0094-35%2C_Balkan%2C_PKW_der_Leibstandarte_Adolf_Hitler.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Bundesarchiv_Bild_101I-158-0094-35%2C_Balkan%2C_PKW_der_Leibstandarte_Adolf_Hitler.jpg/330px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_101I-158-0094-35%2C_Balkan%2C_PKW_der_Leibstandarte_Adolf_Hitler.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Bundesarchiv_Bild_101I-158-0094-35%2C_Balkan%2C_PKW_der_Leibstandarte_Adolf_Hitler.jpg/440px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_101I-158-0094-35%2C_Balkan%2C_PKW_der_Leibstandarte_Adolf_Hitler.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_Bild_101I-158-0094-35,_Balkan,_PKW_der_Leibstandarte_Adolf_Hitler.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/1st_SS_Panzer_Division_Leibstandarte_SS_Adolf_Hitler" title="1st SS Panzer Division Leibstandarte SS Adolf Hitler"><i>Leibstandarte SS Adolf Hitler</i> Division</a> advancing into the <a href="/wiki/Balkans" title="Balkans">Balkans</a> during 1941</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In March 1941, a major <a href="/wiki/Italian_Army" title="Italian Army">Italian</a> counterattack against <a href="/wiki/Greece" title="Greece">Greek</a> forces failed, and Germany came to the aid of its ally. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Operation_Marita" title="Operation Marita">Operation Marita</a> began on 6 April 1941, with German troops invading Greece through <a href="/wiki/Bulgaria" title="Bulgaria">Bulgaria</a> and <a href="/wiki/Yugoslavia" title="Yugoslavia">Yugoslavia</a> in an effort to secure its southern flank.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEvans2008153_56-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEvans2008153-56">[55]</a></sup></p>
<p><i>Reich</i> was ordered to leave France and head for <a href="/wiki/Romania" title="Romania">Romania</a>, and the <i>Leibstandarte</i> was ordered to <a href="/wiki/Bulgaria" title="Bulgaria">Bulgaria</a>. The <i>Leibstandarte</i>, attached to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/XL_Panzer_Corps_(Germany)" title="XL Panzer Corps (Germany)">XL Panzer Corps</a>, advanced west then south from Bulgaria into the mountains, and by 9 April had reached <a href="/wiki/Prilep" title="Prilep">Prilep</a> in Yugoslavia, 30 miles from the Greek border.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFlaherty2004163_57-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFlaherty2004163-57">[56]</a></sup> Further north the SS <i>Reich</i>, with the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/XXXXI_Panzer_Corps_(Germany)" title="XXXXI Panzer Corps (Germany)">XLI Panzer Corps</a>, crossed the Romanian border and advanced on <a href="/wiki/Belgrade" title="Belgrade">Belgrade</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Yugoslavia" title="Kingdom of Yugoslavia">Yugoslav</a> capital. <a href="/wiki/Fritz_Klingenberg" title="Fritz Klingenberg">Fritz Klingenberg</a>, a company commander in the <i>Reich</i>, led his men into Belgrade, where a small group in the vanguard accepted the surrender of the city on 13 April. A few days later the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Yugoslav_Army" title="Royal Yugoslav Army">Royal Yugoslav Army</a> surrendered.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFlaherty2004162.2C_163_58-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFlaherty2004162.2C_163-58">[57]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWeale2012297_59-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWeale2012297-59">[58]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <i>Leibstandarte</i> had now crossed into Greece, and on 10 April engaged the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/6th_Australian_Division" title="6th Australian Division">6th Australian Division</a> in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Battle_of_the_Klidi_Pass" title="Battle of the Klidi Pass">Battle of the Klidi Pass</a>. For 48 hours they fought for control of the heights, often engaging in hand-to-hand combat, eventually gaining control with the capture of Height 997, which opened the pass and allowed the German Army to advance into the Greek interior.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFlaherty2004165_60-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFlaherty2004165-60">[59]</a></sup> This victory gained praise from the OKW: in the order of the day they were commended for their "unshakable offensive spirit" and told that "the present victory signifies for the <i>Leibstandarte</i> a new and imperishable page of honour in its history."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFlaherty2004165_60-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFlaherty2004165-60">[59]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <i>Leibstandarte</i> continued the advance on 13 May. When the Reconnaissance Battalion under the command of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kurt_Meyer_(Panzermeyer)" title="Kurt Meyer (Panzermeyer)">Kurt Meyer</a> came under heavy fire from the Greek Army <a href="/wiki/Capture_of_Klisura_Pass" title="Capture of Klisura Pass">defending the Klisura Pass</a>, they broke through the defenders and captured 1,000 prisoners of war at the cost of six dead and nine wounded.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFlaherty2004165_60-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFlaherty2004165-60">[59]</a></sup> The next day, Meyer captured <a href="/wiki/Kastoria" title="Kastoria">Kastoria</a> and took another 11,000 prisoners of war. By 20 May the <i>Leibstandarte</i> had cut off the retreating Greek Army at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Metsovon" title="Metsovon">Metsovon</a> and accepted the surrender of the Greek Epirus-Macedonian Army.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFlaherty2004165_60-3"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFlaherty2004165-60">[59]</a></sup> As a reward, the <i>Leibstandarte</i> was nominally redesignated as a full motorized division, although few additional elements had been added by the start of the Russian campaign and the "Division" remained effectively a reinforced brigade.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Soviet_Union">Soviet Union</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Waffen-SS&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Soviet Union">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p><a href="/wiki/Operation_Barbarossa" title="Operation Barbarossa">Operation Barbarossa</a>, the German invasion of the Soviet Union, started on 22 June 1941, and all the Waffen-SS formations participated (including the SS <i>Reich</i>, which was formally renamed to SS <i>Das Reich</i> by the Fall of 1941).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEStein1984104_61-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEStein1984104-61">[60]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-A0706-0018-030,_Ukraine,_ermordete_Familie.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="500" data-file-width="800" height="138" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-A0706-0018-030%2C_Ukraine%2C_ermordete_Familie.jpg/220px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-A0706-0018-030%2C_Ukraine%2C_ermordete_Familie.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-A0706-0018-030%2C_Ukraine%2C_ermordete_Familie.jpg/330px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-A0706-0018-030%2C_Ukraine%2C_ermordete_Familie.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-A0706-0018-030%2C_Ukraine%2C_ermordete_Familie.jpg/440px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-A0706-0018-030%2C_Ukraine%2C_ermordete_Familie.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-A0706-0018-030,_Ukraine,_ermordete_Familie.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A boy is forced by SS members to view his murdered family and pose for a photograph before being murdered in <a href="/wiki/Zboriv" title="Zboriv">Zboriv</a>, Ukraine, 1941</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>SS Division <i>Nord</i> in northern <a href="/wiki/Finland" title="Finland">Finland</a> took part in <a href="/wiki/Operation_Arctic_Fox" title="Operation Arctic Fox">Operation Arctic Fox</a> with the Finnish Army and fought at the battle of <a href="/wiki/Salla" title="Salla">Salla</a>, where against strong Soviet forces they suffered 300 killed and 400 wounded in the first two days of the invasion. Thick forests and heavy smoke from forest fires disoriented the troops and the division's units completely fell apart.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWindrowBurn19929_62-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWindrowBurn19929-62">[61]</a></sup> By the end of 1941, <i>Nord</i> had suffered severe casualties. Over the winter of 1941–42 it received replacements from the general pool of Waffen-SS recruits, who were supposedly younger and better trained than the SS men of the original formation, which had been drawn largely from <i>Totenkopfstandarten</i> of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nazi_concentration_camp" title="Nazi concentration camp">Nazi concentration camp</a> guards.</p>
<p>The rest of the Waffen-SS divisions and brigades fared better. The SS <i>Totenkopf</i> and Polizei divisions were attached to <a href="/wiki/Army_Group_North" title="Army Group North">Army Group North</a>, with the mission to advance through the <a href="/wiki/Baltic_states" title="Baltic states">Baltic states</a> and on to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Leningrad" title="Leningrad">Leningrad</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWindrowBurn19927.E2.80.938_22-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWindrowBurn19927.E2.80.938-22">[22]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFlaherty2004166_63-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFlaherty2004166-63">[62]</a></sup> The SS Division <i>Das Reich</i> was with <a href="/wiki/Army_Group_Centre" title="Army Group Centre">Army Group Centre</a> and headed towards <a href="/wiki/Moscow" title="Moscow">Moscow</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWindrowBurn19927.E2.80.938_22-3"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWindrowBurn19927.E2.80.938-22">[22]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFlaherty2004166_63-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFlaherty2004166-63">[62]</a></sup> The SS Division <i>Wiking</i> and the <i>Leibstandarte</i> were with <a href="/wiki/Army_Group_South" title="Army Group South">Army Group South</a>, heading for the <a href="/wiki/Ukraine" title="Ukraine">Ukraine</a> and the city of <a href="/wiki/Kiev" title="Kiev">Kiev</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWindrowBurn19927.E2.80.938_22-4"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWindrowBurn19927.E2.80.938-22">[22]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFlaherty2004166_63-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFlaherty2004166-63">[62]</a></sup></p>
<p>The war in the Soviet Union proceeded well at first, but the cost to the Waffen-SS was extreme: by late October the <i>Leibstandarte</i> was at half strength due to enemy action and <a href="/wiki/Dysentery" title="Dysentery">dysentery</a> that swept through the ranks.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFlaherty2004168_64-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFlaherty2004168-64">[63]</a></sup> <i>Das Reich</i> lost 60% of its strength and was still to take part in the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Moscow" title="Battle of Moscow">Battle of Moscow</a>. The unit was decimated in the following Soviet offensive. The <i>Der Führer</i> Regiment was reduced to 35 men out of the 2,000 that had started the campaign in June.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFlaherty2004168_64-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFlaherty2004168-64">[63]</a></sup> Altogether, the Waffen-SS had suffered 43,000 casualties.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFlaherty2004168_64-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFlaherty2004168-64">[63]</a></sup></p>
<p>While the <i>Leibstandarte</i> and the SS divisions were fighting in the front line, behind the lines it was a different story. The 1 SS Infantry and 2 SS Infantry Brigades, which had been formed from surplus concentration camp guards of the SS-TV, and the SS Cavalry Brigade moved into the Soviet Union behind the advancing armies. At first they fought <a href="/wiki/Soviet_partisans" title="Soviet partisans">Soviet partisans</a> and cut off units of the <a href="/wiki/Red_Army" title="Red Army">Red Army</a> in the rear of <a href="/wiki/Army_Group_South" title="Army Group South">Army Group South</a>, capturing 7,000 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Prisoners_of_war" title="Prisoners of war">prisoners of war</a>, but from mid-August 1941 until late 1942 they were assigned to the <a href="/wiki/Reich_Main_Security_Office" title="Reich Main Security Office">Reich Main Security Office</a> headed by <a href="/wiki/Reinhard_Heydrich" title="Reinhard Heydrich">Reinhard Heydrich</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWindrowBurn19929_62-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWindrowBurn19929-62">[61]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHannesNaumann2000136_65-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHannesNaumann2000136-65">[64]</a></sup> The brigades were now used for rear area security and policing, and were no longer under army or Waffen-SS command. In the Autumn of 1941, they left the anti-partisan role to other units and actively took part in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Holocaust" title="Holocaust">Holocaust</a>. While assisting the <i><a href="/wiki/Einsatzgruppen" title="Einsatzgruppen">Einsatzgruppen</a></i>, they participated in the extermination of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jewish" title="Jewish">Jewish</a> population of the Soviet Union, forming firing parties when required. The three brigades were responsible for the murder of tens of thousands by the end of 1941.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHannesNaumann2000136_65-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHannesNaumann2000136-65">[64]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_Bild_101III-Adendorff-002-18A,_Russland,_SS-Kavallerie-Brigade.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="522" data-file-width="800" height="144" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Bundesarchiv_Bild_101III-Adendorff-002-18A%2C_Russland%2C_SS-Kavallerie-Brigade.jpg/220px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_101III-Adendorff-002-18A%2C_Russland%2C_SS-Kavallerie-Brigade.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Bundesarchiv_Bild_101III-Adendorff-002-18A%2C_Russland%2C_SS-Kavallerie-Brigade.jpg/330px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_101III-Adendorff-002-18A%2C_Russland%2C_SS-Kavallerie-Brigade.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Bundesarchiv_Bild_101III-Adendorff-002-18A%2C_Russland%2C_SS-Kavallerie-Brigade.jpg/440px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_101III-Adendorff-002-18A%2C_Russland%2C_SS-Kavallerie-Brigade.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_Bild_101III-Adendorff-002-18A,_Russland,_SS-Kavallerie-Brigade.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Cavalrymen of the <a href="/wiki/SS_Cavalry_Brigade" title="SS Cavalry Brigade">SS Cavalry Brigade</a>. September 1941.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Because it was more mobile and better able to carry out large-scale operations, the SS Cavalry Brigade had 2 regiments with a strength of 3500 men and played a pivotal role in the transition to the wholesale extermination of the Jewish population.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBrowning2007279_66-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBrowning2007279-66">[65]</a></sup> In the summer of 1941, Himmler assigned <a href="/wiki/Hermann_Fegelein" title="Hermann Fegelein">Hermann Fegelein</a> to be in charge of both regiments.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPieper201552.E2.80.9353_67-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPieper201552.E2.80.9353-67">[66]</a></sup> On 19 July 1941 Himmler assigned Fegelein's regiments to the general command of HSSPF <a href="/wiki/Erich_von_dem_Bach-Zelewski" title="Erich von dem Bach-Zelewski">Erich von dem Bach-Zelewski</a> for the "systematic combing" of the <a href="/wiki/Pripyat_swamps_(punitive_operation)" title="Pripyat swamps (punitive operation)">Pripyat swamps</a>, an operation designed to round up and exterminate <a href="/wiki/Jews" title="Jews">Jews</a>, partisans, and civilians in that area of <a href="/wiki/Byelorussian_Soviet_Socialist_Republic" title="Byelorussian Soviet Socialist Republic">Byelorussian SSR</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPieper201562.2C_80_68-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPieper201562.2C_80-68">[67]</a></sup></p>
<p>Fegelein split the territory to be covered into two sections divided by the <a href="/wiki/Pripyat_River" title="Pripyat River">Pripyat River</a>, with the 1st Regiment taking the northern half and the 2nd Regiment the south.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPieper201581_69-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPieper201581-69">[68]</a></sup> The regiments worked their way from east to west through their assigned territory, and filed daily reports on the number of people killed and taken prisoner. By 1 August the SS Cavalry Regiment 1 under the command of <a href="/wiki/Gustav_Lombard" title="Gustav Lombard">Gustav Lombard</a> was responsible for the death of 800 people; by 6 August, this total had reached 3,000 "Jews and partisans".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBrowning2007280_70-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBrowning2007280-70">[69]</a></sup> Throughout the following weeks, personnel of SS Cavalry Regiment 1 under Lombard's command murdered an estimated 11,000 Jews and more than 400 dispersed soldiers of the Red Army.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECuppers2006279_71-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECuppers2006279-71">[70]</a></sup> Thus Fegelein's units were among the first in the Holocaust to wipe out entire Jewish communities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPieper201586.2C_88.E2.80.9389_72-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPieper201586.2C_88.E2.80.9389-72">[71]</a></sup> Fegelein's final operational report dated 18 September 1941, states that they killed 14,178 Jews, 1,001 partisans, 699 Red Army soldiers, with 830 prisoners taken and losses of 17 dead, 36 wounded, and 3 missing.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPieper2015119.E2.80.93120_73-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPieper2015119.E2.80.93120-73">[72]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMiller2006310_74-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMiller2006310-74">[73]</a></sup> Historian Henning Pieper estimates the actual number of Jews killed was closer to 23,700.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPieper2015120_75-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPieper2015120-75">[74]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1942">1942</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Waffen-SS&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: 1942">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="1942_expansion">1942 expansion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Waffen-SS&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: 1942 expansion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>

</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_Bild_146-1977-143-15,_Russland,_Angeh%C3%B6rige_der_Waffen-SS.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="576" data-file-width="800" height="158" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Bundesarchiv_Bild_146-1977-143-15%2C_Russland%2C_Angeh%C3%B6rige_der_Waffen-SS.jpg/220px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_146-1977-143-15%2C_Russland%2C_Angeh%C3%B6rige_der_Waffen-SS.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Bundesarchiv_Bild_146-1977-143-15%2C_Russland%2C_Angeh%C3%B6rige_der_Waffen-SS.jpg/330px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_146-1977-143-15%2C_Russland%2C_Angeh%C3%B6rige_der_Waffen-SS.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Bundesarchiv_Bild_146-1977-143-15%2C_Russland%2C_Angeh%C3%B6rige_der_Waffen-SS.jpg/440px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_146-1977-143-15%2C_Russland%2C_Angeh%C3%B6rige_der_Waffen-SS.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_Bild_146-1977-143-15,_Russland,_Angeh%C3%B6rige_der_Waffen-SS.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/3rd_SS_Division" title="3rd SS Division">3rd SS Division</a> on the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Front_(World_War_II)" title="Eastern Front (World War II)">Eastern Front</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 1942, the Waffen-SS was further expanded and a new division was entered on the rolls in March. By the second half of 1942 an increasing number of foreigners, many of whom were not volunteers, began entering the ranks.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEStein1984171_76-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEStein1984171-76">[75]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/7th_SS_Volunteer_Mountain_Division_Prinz_Eugen" title="7th SS Volunteer Mountain Division Prinz Eugen">7th SS Volunteer Mountain Division <i>Prinz Eugen</i></a> was recruited from <a href="/wiki/Volksdeutsche" title="Volksdeutsche">Volksdeutsche</a> (ethnic Germans) drafted under threat of punishment by the local German leadership<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEStein1984171_76-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEStein1984171-76">[75]</a></sup> from <a href="/wiki/Croatia" title="Croatia">Croatia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Serbia" title="Serbia">Serbia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hungary" title="Hungary">Hungary</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Romania" title="Romania">Romania</a> and used for anti-partisan operations in the Balkans.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWindrowBurn19929_62-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWindrowBurn19929-62">[61]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMitcham2007148_77-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMitcham2007148-77">[76]</a></sup> Himmler approved the introduction of formal compulsory service for the Volksdeutsche in German occupied Serbia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEStein1984171_76-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEStein1984171-76">[75]</a></sup> Another new division was formed at the same time, when the SS Cavalry Brigade was used as the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/En_cadre" title="En cadre">cadre</a> in the formation of the <a href="/wiki/8th_SS_Cavalry_Division_Florian_Geyer" title="8th SS Cavalry Division Florian Geyer">8th SS Cavalry Division <i>Florian Geyer</i></a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWindrowBurn19929_62-3"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWindrowBurn19929-62">[61]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Panzergrenadier_divisions">Panzergrenadier divisions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Waffen-SS&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Panzergrenadier divisions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The front line divisions of the Waffen-SS that had suffered losses through the winter of 1941–1942 and during the Soviet counter-offensive were withdrawn to France to recover and be reformed as <a href="/wiki/Panzergrenadier" title="Panzergrenadier">Panzergrenadier</a> divisions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEReynolds19979_78-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEReynolds19979-78">[77]</a></sup> Due to the efforts of Himmler and <i><a href="/wiki/Obergruppenf%C3%BChrer" title="Obergruppenführer">Obergruppenführer</a></i> <a href="/wiki/Paul_Hausser" title="Paul Hausser">Paul Hausser</a>, the new commander of the <a href="/wiki/II_SS_Panzer_Corps" title="II SS Panzer Corps">SS Panzer Corps</a>, the three SS Panzergrenadier divisions <i>Leibstandarte</i>, <i>Das Reich</i>, and <i>Totenkopf</i> were to be formed with a full regiment of tanks rather than only a battalion. This meant that the SS Panzergrenadier divisions were full-strength Panzer divisions in all but name. They each received nine <a href="/wiki/Tiger_I" title="Tiger I">Tiger tanks</a>, which were formed into the <a href="/wiki/German_heavy_tank_battalion#Performance_of_the_Tiger_Battalions_in_Action" title="German heavy tank battalion">heavy panzer companies</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEReynolds19979_78-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEReynolds19979-78">[77]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Demyansk_Pocket">Demyansk Pocket</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Waffen-SS&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Demyansk Pocket">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The Soviet offensive of January 1942 trapped a number of German divisions in the <a href="/wiki/Demyansk_Pocket" title="Demyansk Pocket">Demyansk Pocket</a> between February and April 1942; the 3rd SS <i>Totenkopf</i> was one of the divisions encircled by the Red Army. The Red Army liberated <a href="/wiki/Demyansk" title="Demyansk">Demyansk</a> on 1 March 1943 with the retreat of the German troops. "For his excellence in command and the particularly fierce fighting of the <i>Totenkopf</i>", <i><a href="/wiki/Obergruppenf%C3%BChrer" title="Obergruppenführer">Obergruppenführer</a></i> <a href="/wiki/Theodor_Eicke" title="Theodor Eicke">Theodor Eicke</a> was awarded the Oak Leaves to the <a href="/wiki/Knight%27s_Cross_of_the_Iron_Cross" title="Knight's Cross of the Iron Cross">Knight's Cross</a> on 20 May 1942.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFellgiebel200059_79-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFellgiebel200059-79">[78]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1943">1943</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Waffen-SS&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: 1943">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="1943_expansion">1943 expansion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Waffen-SS&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: 1943 expansion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_Bild_146-1974-059-40,_Amin_al_Husseini_bei_bosnischen_SS-Freiwilligen.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="581" data-file-width="800" height="160" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Bundesarchiv_Bild_146-1974-059-40%2C_Amin_al_Husseini_bei_bosnischen_SS-Freiwilligen.jpg/220px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_146-1974-059-40%2C_Amin_al_Husseini_bei_bosnischen_SS-Freiwilligen.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Bundesarchiv_Bild_146-1974-059-40%2C_Amin_al_Husseini_bei_bosnischen_SS-Freiwilligen.jpg/330px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_146-1974-059-40%2C_Amin_al_Husseini_bei_bosnischen_SS-Freiwilligen.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Bundesarchiv_Bild_146-1974-059-40%2C_Amin_al_Husseini_bei_bosnischen_SS-Freiwilligen.jpg/440px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_146-1974-059-40%2C_Amin_al_Husseini_bei_bosnischen_SS-Freiwilligen.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_Bild_146-1974-059-40,_Amin_al_Husseini_bei_bosnischen_SS-Freiwilligen.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Propaganda photo of Grand Mufti of Jerusalem, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Haj_Amin_al-Husseini" title="Haj Amin al-Husseini">Haj Amin al-Husseini</a> inspecting Bosnian <a href="/wiki/13th_Waffen_Mountain_Division_of_the_SS_Handschar_(1st_Croatian)" title="13th Waffen Mountain Division of the SS Handschar (1st Croatian)">Waffen-SS</a> recruits, November 1943</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The Waffen-SS expanded further in 1943: in February the <a href="/wiki/9th_SS_Panzer_Division_Hohenstaufen" title="9th SS Panzer Division Hohenstaufen">9th SS Panzer Division <i>Hohenstaufen</i></a> and its sister division, the <a href="/wiki/10th_SS_Panzer_Division_Frundsberg" title="10th SS Panzer Division Frundsberg">10th SS Panzer Division <i>Frundsberg</i></a>, were formed in France. They were followed in July by the <a href="/wiki/11th_SS_Volunteer_Panzergrenadier_Division_Nordland" title="11th SS Volunteer Panzergrenadier Division Nordland">11th SS Volunteer Panzergrenadier Division <i>Nordland</i></a> created from Norwegian and Danish volunteers. September saw the formation of the <a href="/wiki/12th_SS_Panzer_Division_Hitlerjugend" title="12th SS Panzer Division Hitlerjugend">12th SS Panzer Division <i>Hitlerjugend</i></a> using volunteers from the <a href="/wiki/Hitler_Youth" title="Hitler Youth">Hitler Youth</a>. Himmler and Berger successfully appealed to Hitler to form a <a href="/wiki/Bosniaks" title="Bosniaks">Bosnian</a> <a href="/wiki/Muslim" title="Muslim">Muslim</a> division, and the <a href="/wiki/13th_Waffen_Mountain_Division_of_the_SS_Handschar_(1st_Croatian)" title="13th Waffen Mountain Division of the SS Handschar (1st Croatian)">13th Waffen Mountain Division of the SS Handschar (1st Croatian)</a>, the first non-Germanic division, was formed, to fight <a href="/wiki/Josip_Broz_Tito" title="Josip Broz Tito">Josip Broz Tito</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Yugoslav_Partisans" title="Yugoslav Partisans">Yugoslav Partisans</a>. This was followed by the <a href="/wiki/14th_Waffen_Grenadier_Division_of_the_SS_(1st_Galician)" title="14th Waffen Grenadier Division of the SS (1st Galician)">14th Waffen Grenadier Division of the SS (1st Galician)</a> formed from volunteers from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Galicia_(Central_Europe)" title="Galicia (Central Europe)">Galicia</a> in western <a href="/wiki/Ukraine" title="Ukraine">Ukraine</a>. The <a href="/wiki/15th_Waffen_Grenadier_Division_of_the_SS_(1st_Latvian)" title="15th Waffen Grenadier Division of the SS (1st Latvian)">15th Waffen Grenadier Division of the SS (1st Latvian)</a> was created in 1943, using compulsory military service in the <a href="/wiki/Reichskommissariat_Ostland" title="Reichskommissariat Ostland">Ostland</a>. The final new 1943 division was the <a href="/wiki/16th_SS_Panzergrenadier_Division_Reichsf%C3%BChrer-SS" title="16th SS Panzergrenadier Division Reichsführer-SS">16th SS Panzergrenadier Division <i>Reichsführer-SS</i></a>, which was created using the <a href="/wiki/Sturmbrigade_Reichsf%C3%BChrer_SS" title="Sturmbrigade Reichsführer SS">Sturmbrigade Reichsführer SS</a> as a cadre. By the end of the year, the Waffen-SS had increased in size from eight divisions and some brigades to 16 divisions.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Kharkov">Kharkov</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Waffen-SS&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Kharkov">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_Bild_101III-Zschaeckel-189-13,_Russland,_Charkow,_Waffen-SS_mit_Panzer_IV.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="551" data-file-width="800" height="117" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Bundesarchiv_Bild_101III-Zschaeckel-189-13%2C_Russland%2C_Charkow%2C_Waffen-SS_mit_Panzer_IV.jpg/170px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_101III-Zschaeckel-189-13%2C_Russland%2C_Charkow%2C_Waffen-SS_mit_Panzer_IV.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Bundesarchiv_Bild_101III-Zschaeckel-189-13%2C_Russland%2C_Charkow%2C_Waffen-SS_mit_Panzer_IV.jpg/255px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_101III-Zschaeckel-189-13%2C_Russland%2C_Charkow%2C_Waffen-SS_mit_Panzer_IV.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Bundesarchiv_Bild_101III-Zschaeckel-189-13%2C_Russland%2C_Charkow%2C_Waffen-SS_mit_Panzer_IV.jpg/340px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_101III-Zschaeckel-189-13%2C_Russland%2C_Charkow%2C_Waffen-SS_mit_Panzer_IV.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_Bild_101III-Zschaeckel-189-13,_Russland,_Charkow,_Waffen-SS_mit_Panzer_IV.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
German tanks at Kharkov, 1943</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>On the Eastern Front, the Germans suffered a devastating defeat when the <a href="/wiki/6th_Army_(Wehrmacht)" title="6th Army (Wehrmacht)">6th Army</a> was defeated during the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Stalingrad" title="Battle of Stalingrad">Battle of Stalingrad</a>.
