Hitler ordered the SS Panzer Corps back to the Eastern Front for a counter-attack with the city of <a href="/wiki/Kharkiv" title="Kharkiv">Kharkiv</a> as its objective.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFlaherty2004173_80-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFlaherty2004173-80">[79]</a></sup> The SS Panzer Corps was in full retreat on 19 February, having been attacked by the <a href="/wiki/6th_Army_(Soviet_Union)" title="6th Army (Soviet Union)">Soviet 6th Army</a>, when they received the order to counter-attack.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFlaherty2004173_80-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFlaherty2004173-80">[79]</a></sup> Disobeying Hitler's order to "stand fast and fight to the death", Hausser withdrew in front of the Red Army. During <a href="/wiki/Manstein" title="Manstein">Manstein</a>'s counteroffensive, the SS Panzer Corps, without support from the <a href="/wiki/Luftwaffe" title="Luftwaffe">Luftwaffe</a> or neighbouring German formations, broke through the Soviet line and advanced on Kharkov.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFlaherty2004173.E2.80.93174_81-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFlaherty2004173.E2.80.93174-81">[80]</a></sup> Despite orders to encircle Kharkov from the north, the SS Panzer Corps directly attacked in the <a href="/wiki/Third_Battle_of_Kharkov" title="Third Battle of Kharkov">Third Battle of Kharkov</a> on 11 March.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMargry200120_82-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMargry200120-82">[81]</a></sup> This led to four days of house-to-house fighting before Kharkov was recaptured by the SS Division Leibstandarte on 15 March. Two days later the German forces recaptured <a href="/wiki/Belgorod" title="Belgorod">Belgorod</a>, creating the <a href="/wiki/Salients,_re-entrants_and_pockets" title="Salients, re-entrants and pockets">salient</a> that in July 1943 led to the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Kursk" title="Battle of Kursk">Battle of Kursk</a>. The German offensive cost the Red Army an estimated 70,000 <a href="/wiki/Casualty_(person)" title="Casualty (person)">casualties</a> but the house-to-house fighting in Kharkov was particularly bloody for the SS Panzer Corps, which lost approximately 44% of its strength by the time operations ended in late March.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEReynolds199710_83-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEReynolds199710-83">[82]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Warsaw_Ghetto_uprising">Warsaw Ghetto uprising</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Waffen-SS&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Warsaw Ghetto uprising">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Stroop_Report_-_Warsaw_Ghetto_Uprising_03.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1289" data-file-width="1868" height="152" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Stroop_Report_-_Warsaw_Ghetto_Uprising_03.jpg/220px-Stroop_Report_-_Warsaw_Ghetto_Uprising_03.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Stroop_Report_-_Warsaw_Ghetto_Uprising_03.jpg/330px-Stroop_Report_-_Warsaw_Ghetto_Uprising_03.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Stroop_Report_-_Warsaw_Ghetto_Uprising_03.jpg/440px-Stroop_Report_-_Warsaw_Ghetto_Uprising_03.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Stroop_Report_-_Warsaw_Ghetto_Uprising_03.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Stroop_Report" title="Stroop Report">Stroop Report</a> original caption: "The leader of the grand operation." SS-<a href="/wiki/Brigadef%C3%BChrer" title="Brigadeführer">Brigadeführer</a> <a href="/wiki/J%C3%BCrgen_Stroop" title="Jürgen Stroop">Jürgen Stroop</a> (center) watches housing blocks burn.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Warsaw_Ghetto_Uprising" title="Warsaw Ghetto Uprising">Warsaw Ghetto Uprising</a> was a Jewish <a href="/wiki/Insurgency" title="Insurgency">insurgency</a> that arose within the <a href="/wiki/Warsaw_Ghetto" title="Warsaw Ghetto">Warsaw Ghetto</a> from 19 April to 16 May, an effort to prevent the transportation of the remaining population of the ghetto to <a href="/wiki/Treblinka_extermination_camp" title="Treblinka extermination camp">Treblinka extermination camp</a>. Units involved from the Waffen-SS were 821 Waffen-SS <a href="/wiki/Panzergrenadier" title="Panzergrenadier">Panzergrenadiers</a> from five reserve and training battalions and one cavalry reserve and training battalion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEStroop1943_84-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEStroop1943-84">[83]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHolocaust_Memorial_Museum_85-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHolocaust_Memorial_Museum-85">[84]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Kursk">Kursk</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Waffen-SS&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Kursk">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>For the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Kursk" title="Battle of Kursk">Battle of Kursk</a>, the SS Panzer Corps was renamed the <a href="/wiki/II_SS_Panzer_Corps" title="II SS Panzer Corps">II SS Panzer Corps</a> and was part of the <a href="/wiki/4th_Panzer_Army" title="4th Panzer Army">4th Panzer Army</a>. The II SS Panzer Corps spearheaded the attack through the Soviet defenses. The attack penetrated to a depth of 35 kilometres (22 mi) and was then stopped by the <a href="/wiki/1st_Guards_Tank_Army_(Soviet_Union)" title="1st Guards Tank Army (Soviet Union)">Soviet 1st Tank Army</a>.</p>
<p>The Soviet reserves had been sent south to defend against a German attack by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/III_Panzer_Corps" title="III Panzer Corps">III Panzer Corps</a>. With the loss of their reserves, any hope they may have had of dealing a major defeat to the SS Panzer Corps ended. But the German advances now failed – despite appalling losses, the Soviet tank armies held the line and prevented the II SS Panzer Corps from making the expected breakthrough.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBergstrom200781_86-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBergstrom200781-86">[85]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_Bild_101III-Zschaeckel-207-12,_Schlacht_um_Kursk,_Panzer_VI_(Tiger_I).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="495" data-file-width="800" height="136" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Bundesarchiv_Bild_101III-Zschaeckel-207-12%2C_Schlacht_um_Kursk%2C_Panzer_VI_%28Tiger_I%29.jpg/220px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_101III-Zschaeckel-207-12%2C_Schlacht_um_Kursk%2C_Panzer_VI_%28Tiger_I%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Bundesarchiv_Bild_101III-Zschaeckel-207-12%2C_Schlacht_um_Kursk%2C_Panzer_VI_%28Tiger_I%29.jpg/330px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_101III-Zschaeckel-207-12%2C_Schlacht_um_Kursk%2C_Panzer_VI_%28Tiger_I%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Bundesarchiv_Bild_101III-Zschaeckel-207-12%2C_Schlacht_um_Kursk%2C_Panzer_VI_%28Tiger_I%29.jpg/440px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_101III-Zschaeckel-207-12%2C_Schlacht_um_Kursk%2C_Panzer_VI_%28Tiger_I%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_Bild_101III-Zschaeckel-207-12,_Schlacht_um_Kursk,_Panzer_VI_(Tiger_I).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Tiger_I" title="Tiger I">Tiger tank Company</a> <i><a href="/wiki/2nd_SS_Panzer_Division_Das_Reich" title="2nd SS Panzer Division Das Reich">Das Reich</a></i> during the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Kursk" title="Battle of Kursk">Battle of Kursk</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The failure to break through the Soviet tactical zone and the need to break off the assault by the German 9th Army on the northern shoulder of the Kursk salient due to <a href="/wiki/Operation_Kutuzov" title="Operation Kutuzov">Operation Kutuzov</a> contributed to Hitler's decision to halt the offensive. A parallel attack by the Red Army against the new 6th Army on the Mius river south of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kharkov" title="Kharkov">Kharkov</a> necessitated the withdrawal of reserve forces held to exploit any success on the southern shoulder of Kursk. The OKW also had to draw on some German troops from the Eastern Front to bolster the Mediterranean theatre following the Anglo-American <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Invasion_of_Sicily" title="Invasion of Sicily">Invasion of Sicily</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFritz2011350_87-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFritz2011350-87">[86]</a></sup> On 17 July Hitler called off the operation and ordered a withdrawal.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEvans2008488.E2.80.93489_88-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEvans2008488.E2.80.93489-88">[87]</a></sup> The Soviet Union was not beaten, and the strategic initiative had swung to the Red Army. The Germans were forced onto the defensive as the Red Army began the liberation of Western Russia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcNab200968.2C_70_89-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcNab200968.2C_70-89">[88]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Italy">Italy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Waffen-SS&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Italy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The <i>Leibstandarte</i> was thereafter sent to Italy to help stabilise the situation there caused by the deposal of <a href="/wiki/Benito_Mussolini" title="Benito Mussolini">Benito Mussolini</a> by the <a href="/wiki/Pietro_Badoglio" title="Pietro Badoglio">Badoglio</a> government and the Allied Sicily invasion, which was the beginning of the <a href="/wiki/Italian_Campaign_(World_War_II)" title="Italian Campaign (World War II)">Italian Campaign</a>. The division left behind its armour and equipment, which was given to <i>Das Reich</i> and <i>Totenkopf</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEReynolds199715_90-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEReynolds199715-90">[89]</a></sup> After the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Armistice_between_Italy_and_Allied_armed_forces" title="Armistice between Italy and Allied armed forces">Italian surrender</a> and collapse of 8 September 1943, the <i>Leibstandarte</i> was ordered to begin disarming nearby Italian units.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEReynolds199715_90-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEReynolds199715-90">[89]</a></sup> It also had the task of guarding vital road and rail junctions in the north of Italy and was involved in several skirmishes with partisans.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEReynolds199715_90-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEReynolds199715-90">[89]</a></sup> This went smoothly, with the exception of a brief skirmish with Italian troops stationed in <a href="/wiki/Parma" title="Parma">Parma</a> on 9 September. By 19 September all Italian forces in the <a href="/wiki/Po_Valley" title="Po Valley">Po River plain</a> had been disarmed, but the OKW received reports that elements of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Italian_Fourth_Army" title="Italian Fourth Army">Italian Fourth Army</a> were regrouping in <a href="/wiki/Piedmont" title="Piedmont">Piedmont</a>, near the French border. <a href="/wiki/Joachim_Peiper" title="Joachim Peiper">Joachim Peiper</a>'s mechanised III Battalion, SS Panzergrenadier Regiment 2, was sent to disarm these units.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEReynolds199715_90-3"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEReynolds199715-90">[89]</a></sup> On arriving in the province of <a href="/wiki/Cuneo" title="Cuneo">Cuneo</a>, Peiper was met by an Italian officer who warned that his forces would attack unless Peiper's unit vacated the province immediately. After Peiper refused, the Italians attacked. Peiper's battalion defeated the Italians, and subsequently shelled and burnt down the village of <a href="/wiki/Boves,_Piedmont" title="Boves, Piedmont">Boves</a>, killing at least 34 civilians.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBishopWilliams200398_91-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBishopWilliams200398-91">[90]</a></sup> Peiper's battalion then disarmed the remaining Italian forces in the area.</p>
<p>While the <i>Leibstandarte</i> was operating in the north, the 16 SS <i>Reichsführer</i>-SS sent a <a href="/wiki/Kampfgruppe" title="Kampfgruppe">Kampfgruppe</a> to contain the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Operation_Shingle" title="Operation Shingle">Anzio landings</a> in January 1944. In March, the bulk of the 1st Italienische Freiwilligen Sturmbrigade (or <i>Brigata d'Assalto, Volontari</i> in Italian) was sent to the Anzio beachhead, where they fought alongside their German allies, receiving favourable reports and taking heavy losses. In recognition of their performance, Himmler declared the unit to be fully integrated into the Waffen-SS.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1944">1944</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Waffen-SS&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: 1944">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="1944_expansion">1944 expansion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Waffen-SS&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: 1944 expansion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-J16696,_Soldaten_der_Legion_%22Freies_Indien%22.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="559" data-file-width="800" height="154" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-J16696%2C_Soldaten_der_Legion_%22Freies_Indien%22.jpg/220px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-J16696%2C_Soldaten_der_Legion_%22Freies_Indien%22.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-J16696%2C_Soldaten_der_Legion_%22Freies_Indien%22.jpg/330px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-J16696%2C_Soldaten_der_Legion_%22Freies_Indien%22.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-J16696%2C_Soldaten_der_Legion_%22Freies_Indien%22.jpg/440px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-J16696%2C_Soldaten_der_Legion_%22Freies_Indien%22.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-J16696,_Soldaten_der_Legion_%22Freies_Indien%22.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
After D-Day, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Indische_Legion" title="Indische Legion">Indische Legion</a> was transferred from the Heer to Waffen-SS.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEThomson2004_92-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEThomson2004-92">[91]</a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The Waffen-SS expanded again during 1944. January saw the formation of the <a href="/wiki/19th_Waffen_Grenadier_Division_of_the_SS_(2nd_Latvian)" title="19th Waffen Grenadier Division of the SS (2nd Latvian)">19th Waffen Grenadier Division of the SS (2nd Latvian)</a>, formed from the two SS Infantry Brigades as cadre with Latvian conscripts. The <a href="/wiki/20th_Waffen_Grenadier_Division_of_the_SS_(1st_Estonian)" title="20th Waffen Grenadier Division of the SS (1st Estonian)">20th Waffen Grenadier Division of the SS (1st Estonian)</a> was formed via general conscription in February 1944, around a cadre from the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/3_Estonian_SS_Volunteer_Brigade" title="3 Estonian SS Volunteer Brigade">3 Estonian SS Volunteer Brigade</a>. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/21st_Waffen_Mountain_Division_of_the_SS_Skanderbeg_(1st_Albanian)" title="21st Waffen Mountain Division of the SS Skanderbeg (1st Albanian)">21st Waffen Mountain Division of the SS Skanderbeg (1st Albanian)</a> was formed in March 1944 from Albanian and Kosovan volunteers, which as with other "eastern formations" were intended for use against "irregular forces".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEStein1984184.2C_185.2C_194_93-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEStein1984184.2C_185.2C_194-93">[92]</a></sup> A second Waffen-SS cavalry division followed in April 1944, the <a href="/wiki/22nd_SS_Volunteer_Cavalry_Division_Maria_Theresia" title="22nd SS Volunteer Cavalry Division Maria Theresia">22nd SS Volunteer Cavalry Division <i>Maria Theresia</i></a>. The bulk of the troops were <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Military_of_Hungary" title="Military of Hungary">Hungarian Army</a> Volksdeutsche conscripts transferred to the Waffen-SS following an agreement between Germany and Hungary. The <a href="/wiki/23rd_SS_Volunteer_Panzer_Grenadier_Division_Nederland" title="23rd SS Volunteer Panzer Grenadier Division Nederland">23rd SS Volunteer Panzer Grenadier Division <i>Nederland</i></a> followed, formed from the 4th SS Volunteer Panzergrenadier Brigade Nederland, but it was never more than a large brigade. The <a href="/wiki/24th_Waffen_Mountain_Division_of_the_SS_Karstj%C3%A4ger" title="24th Waffen Mountain Division of the SS Karstjäger">24th Waffen Mountain Division of the SS Karstjäger</a> was another division that was never more than brigade size, consisting mainly of ethnic German volunteers from Italy and Yugoslavia, along with volunteers from Slovenia, Croatia, Serbia, and Ukraine. They were primarily involved in fighting partisans in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kras" title="Kras">Kras</a> region of the <a href="/wiki/Alps" title="Alps">Alps</a> on the frontiers of <a href="/wiki/Slovenia" title="Slovenia">Slovenia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">Italy</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Austria" title="Austria">Austria</a>, the mountainous terrain requiring specialized mountain troops and equipment.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWilliamsonAndrew20044_94-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWilliamsonAndrew20044-94">[93]</a></sup> Two <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hungarian_people" title="Hungarian people">Hungarian</a> divisions followed: the <a href="/wiki/25th_Waffen_Grenadier_Division_of_the_SS_Hunyadi_(1st_Hungarian)" title="25th Waffen Grenadier Division of the SS Hunyadi (1st Hungarian)">25th Waffen Grenadier Division of the SS Hunyadi (1st Hungarian)</a> and the <a href="/wiki/26th_Waffen_Grenadier_Division_of_the_SS_(2nd_Hungarian)" title="26th Waffen Grenadier Division of the SS (2nd Hungarian)">26th Waffen Grenadier Division of the SS (2nd Hungarian)</a>. These were formed under the authority of the Hungarian defense minister, at the request of Himmler. One regiment from the Hungarian Army was ordered to join, but they mostly consisted of Hungarian and Romanian volunteers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWilliamsonAndrew20045.E2.80.936_95-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWilliamsonAndrew20045.E2.80.936-95">[94]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/SS_Division_Langemarck" title="SS Division Langemarck">SS Division Langemarck</a> was formed next in October 1944, from <a href="/wiki/Flanders" title="Flanders">Flemish</a> volunteers added to the 6th SS Volunteer Sturmbrigade Langemarck, but again it was nothing more than a large brigade. The 5th SS Volunteer Sturmbrigade Wallonien was also upgraded to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/SS_Division_Wallonien" title="SS Division Wallonien">SS Division Wallonien</a>, but it too was never more than a large brigade. Plans to convert the Kaminnski Brigade into the <a href="/wiki/29th_Waffen_Grenadier_Division_of_the_SS_RONA_(1st_Russian)" title="29th Waffen Grenadier Division of the SS RONA (1st Russian)">29th Waffen Grenadier Division of the SS RONA (1st Russian)</a> were dropped after the execution of their commander, <a href="/wiki/Bronislav_Kaminski" title="Bronislav Kaminski">Bronislav Kaminski</a>; instead the Waffen Grenadier Brigade of SS (Italian no. 1) became the <a href="/wiki/29th_Waffen_Grenadier_Division_of_the_SS_(1st_Italian)" title="29th Waffen Grenadier Division of the SS (1st Italian)">29th Waffen Grenadier Division of the SS (1st Italian)</a>. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/30th_Waffen_Grenadier_Division_of_the_SS_(2nd_Russian)" title="30th Waffen Grenadier Division of the SS (2nd Russian)">30th Waffen Grenadier Division of the SS (2nd Russian)</a> was formed from the Schutzmannschaft-Brigade Siegling. The final new division of 1944, was the <a href="/wiki/31st_SS_Volunteer_Grenadier_Division" title="31st SS Volunteer Grenadier Division">31st SS Volunteer Grenadier Division</a>, formed from conscripted Volksdeutsche, mainly from the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Batschka" title="Batschka">Batschka</a> region of Hungary.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Korsun-Cherkassy_Pocket">Korsun-Cherkassy Pocket</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Waffen-SS&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Korsun-Cherkassy Pocket">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Korsun-Cherkassy_Pocket" title="Korsun-Cherkassy Pocket">Korsun-Cherkassy Pocket</a> was formed in January 1944 when units of the <a href="/wiki/8th_Army_(Wehrmacht)" title="8th Army (Wehrmacht)">8th Army</a> withdrew to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Panther-Wotan_Line" title="Panther-Wotan Line">Panther-Wotan Line</a>, a defensive position along the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dnieper_River" title="Dnieper River">Dnieper River</a> in Ukraine. Two army corps were left holding a <a href="/wiki/Salients,_re-entrants_and_pockets" title="Salients, re-entrants and pockets">salient</a> into the Soviet lines extending some 100 kilometres (62 mi). The Red Army's 1st and 2nd Ukrainian Fronts encircled the pocket. Trapped in the pocket were a total of six German divisions, including the 5 SS <i>Wiking</i>, with the attached <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/5th_SS_Volunteer_Sturmbrigade_Wallonien" title="5th SS Volunteer Sturmbrigade Wallonien">5th SS Volunteer Sturmbrigade Wallonien</a>, and the Estonian SS Battalion <i>Narwa</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEZetterlingFrankson2008335_96-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEZetterlingFrankson2008335-96">[95]</a></sup> The Germans broke out in coordination with other German forces from the outside, including the 1 SS <i>Leibstandarte</i>. Roughly two out of three encircled men successfully escaped the pocket.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENash2002366_97-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENash2002366-97">[96]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Raid_on_Drvar">Raid on Drvar</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Waffen-SS&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Raid on Drvar">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Raid_on_Drvar" title="Raid on Drvar">Raid on Drvar</a>, codenamed <i>Operation Rösselsprung</i>, was an attack by the Waffen-SS and Luftwaffe on the command structure of the Yugoslav partisans. Their objective was the elimination of the partisan-controlled Supreme Headquarters and the capture of Tito. The offensive took place in April and May 1944. The Waffen-SS units involved were the <a href="/wiki/500th_SS_Parachute_Battalion" title="500th SS Parachute Battalion">500th SS Parachute Battalion</a> and the 7 SS <i>Prinz Eugen</i>.</p>
<p>The assault started when a small group parachuted into <a href="/wiki/Drvar" title="Drvar">Drvar</a> to secure landing grounds for the following <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Glider_aircraft" title="Glider aircraft">glider</a> force. The 500th SS Parachute Battalion fought their way to Tito's cave headquarters and exchanged heavy gunfire resulting in numerous casualties on both sides. By the time German forces had penetrated into the cave, Tito had already escaped. At the end of the battle only 200 men of the 500th SS Parachute Battalion remained unwounded.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEyre2006343.E2.80.93376_98-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEyre2006343.E2.80.93376-98">[97]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Baltic_states">Baltic states</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Waffen-SS&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Baltic states">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>In the Baltic states the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Narva_(1944)" title="Battle of Narva (1944)">Battle of Narva</a> started in February. The battle can be divided into two phases: the <a href="/wiki/Battle_for_Narva_Bridgehead" title="Battle for Narva Bridgehead">Battle for Narva Bridgehead</a> from February to July and the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Tannenberg_Line" title="Battle of Tannenberg Line">Battle of Tannenberg Line</a> from July to September. A number of volunteer and conscript Waffen-SS units from Norway, Denmark, the Netherlands, Belgium, and Estonia fought in Narva. The units were all part of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/III_SS_(Germanic)_Panzer_Corps" title="III SS (Germanic) Panzer Corps">III SS (Germanic) Panzer Corps</a> in <a href="/wiki/Army_Group_North" title="Army Group North">Army Group North</a>, which consisted of the 11th SS Panzergrenadier Division <i>Nordland</i>, the 4th SS Volunteer Panzergrenadier Brigade <i>Nederland</i>, the 5th SS Volunteer Sturmbrigade <i>Wallonien</i>, the 6th SS Volunteer Sturmbrigade <i>Langemarck</i>, and the conscript 20th Waffen Grenadier Division of the SS (1st Estonian), under the command of <i><a href="/wiki/Obergruppenf%C3%BChrer" title="Obergruppenführer">Obergruppenführer</a></i> <a href="/wiki/Felix_Steiner" title="Felix Steiner">Felix Steiner</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMitcham2001261.E2.80.93262_99-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMitcham2001261.E2.80.93262-99">[98]</a></sup></p>
<p>Also in Army Group North was the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/VI_SS_Corps" title="VI SS Corps">VI SS Corps</a>, which consisted of the <a href="/wiki/15th_Waffen_Grenadier_Division_of_the_SS_(1st_Latvian)" title="15th Waffen Grenadier Division of the SS (1st Latvian)">15th Waffen Grenadier Division of the SS (1st Latvian)</a> and the <a href="/wiki/19th_Waffen_Grenadier_Division_of_the_SS_(2nd_Latvian)" title="19th Waffen Grenadier Division of the SS (2nd Latvian)">19th Waffen Grenadier Division of the SS (2nd Latvian)</a>. Latvian Waffen SS and German army units held out in the <a href="/wiki/Courland_Pocket" title="Courland Pocket">Courland Pocket</a> until the end of the war.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Normandy">Normandy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Waffen-SS&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Normandy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Operation_Spring.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="521" data-file-width="457" height="251" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Operation_Spring.png/220px-Operation_Spring.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Operation_Spring.png/330px-Operation_Spring.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Operation_Spring.png/440px-Operation_Spring.png 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Operation_Spring.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The starting lines of <a href="/wiki/Operation_Spring" title="Operation Spring">Operation Spring</a>, Waffen-SS units identified are the <i>1 SS</i>, <i>9 SS</i>, <i>10 SS</i>, <i>12 SS</i> Divisions and the 101 and 102 SS Heavy Panzer Battalions</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Operation_Overlord" title="Operation Overlord">Operation Overlord</a>, the Allied <a href="/wiki/Normandy_landings" title="Normandy landings">"D-Day" landings</a> in <a href="/wiki/Normandy" title="Normandy">Normandy</a>, took place on 6 June 1944. In preparation for the expected landings the I SS Panzer Corps <i>Leibstandarte SS Adolf Hitler</i> was moved to <a href="/wiki/Septeuil" title="Septeuil">Septeuil</a> to the west of Paris in April 1944. The Corps had the 1 SS <i>Leibstandarte SS Adolf Hitler</i>, 12 SS <i>Hitlerjugend</i>, the 17 SS <i>Götz von Berlichingen</i> and the Army's <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Panzer-Lehr-Division" title="Panzer-Lehr-Division">Panzer-Lehr-Division</a> divisions assigned to it.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEReynolds1997131_100-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEReynolds1997131-100">[99]</a></sup> The Corps was to form a part of General <a href="/wiki/Leo_Geyr_von_Schweppenburg" title="Leo Geyr von Schweppenburg">Leo Geyr von Schweppenburg</a>'s <a href="/wiki/5th_Panzer_Army" title="5th Panzer Army">Panzer Group West</a>, the Western theatre's armoured reserve.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEReynolds1997131_100-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEReynolds1997131-100">[99]</a></sup> The Corps was restructured on 4 July 1944 and only the 1 SS <i>Leibstandarte</i> and the 12 SS <i>Hitlerjugend</i> remained at strength.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEReynolds1997145_101-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEReynolds1997145-101">[100]</a></sup></p>
<p>After the landings, the first Waffen-SS unit in action was the 12 SS <i>Hitlerjugend</i>, which arrived at the invasion front on 7 June, in the <a href="/wiki/Caen" title="Caen">Caen</a> area. The same day they committed the <a href="/wiki/Ardenne_Abbey_massacre" title="Ardenne Abbey massacre">Ardenne Abbey massacre</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELatimer2001_102-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELatimer2001-102">[101]</a></sup> The next unit to arrive was the 17 SS <i>Götz von Berlichingen</i> on 11 June, which came into contact with the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/101st_Airborne_Division_(United_States)" title="101st Airborne Division (United States)">101st Airborne Division</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTE.27.27G.C3.B6tz_von_Berlichingen.27.27_Diary_103-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTE.27.27G.C3.B6tz_von_Berlichingen.27.27_Diary-103">[102]</a></sup> The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/SS_Heavy_Panzer_Battalion_101" title="SS Heavy Panzer Battalion 101">SS Heavy Panzer Battalion 101</a> arrived next to protect the left wing of the I SS Panzer Corps. The 1 SS <i>Leibstandarte</i> arrived towards the end of the month with lead elements becoming embroiled in the British offensive <a href="/wiki/Operation_Epsom" title="Operation Epsom">Operation Epsom</a>.</p>
<p>The only other Waffen-SS unit in France at this time was the 2 SS <i>Das Reich</i>, in <a href="/wiki/Montauban" title="Montauban">Montauban</a>, north of <a href="/wiki/Toulouse" title="Toulouse">Toulouse</a>. They were ordered north to the landing beaches and on 9 June were responsible for the <a href="/wiki/Tulle_massacre" title="Tulle massacre">Tulle massacre</a>, where 99 men were murdered. The next day they reached <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Oradour-sur-Glane" title="Oradour-sur-Glane">Oradour-sur-Glane</a> and massacred 642 French civilians.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/II_SS_Panzer_Corps" title="II SS Panzer Corps">II SS Panzer Corps</a> consisting of the 9th SS <i>Hohenstaufen</i> and 10th SS <i>Frundsberg</i> divisions and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/SS_Heavy_Panzer_Battalion_102" title="SS Heavy Panzer Battalion 102">SS Heavy Panzer Battalion 102</a> was transferred from the Eastern Front to spearhead an offensive to destroy the Allied beachhead. However, the British launched Operation Epsom and the two divisions were fed piecemeal into the battle, and launched several counterattacks over the following days.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Falaise_Pocket_German_Counterattack.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="577" data-file-width="800" height="159" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Falaise_Pocket_German_Counterattack.png/220px-Falaise_Pocket_German_Counterattack.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Falaise_Pocket_German_Counterattack.png/330px-Falaise_Pocket_German_Counterattack.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Falaise_Pocket_German_Counterattack.png/440px-Falaise_Pocket_German_Counterattack.png 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Falaise_Pocket_German_Counterattack.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
German counterattacks against Canadian-Polish positions on 20 August 1944</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Without any further reinforcements in men or materiel, the Waffen-SS divisions could not stop the Allied advance. 1 SS <i>Leibstandarte</i> and 2 SS <i>Das Reich</i> took part in the failed <a href="/wiki/Operation_L%C3%BCttich" title="Operation Lüttich">Operation Lüttich</a> in early August.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFey2003145_104-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFey2003145-104">[103]</a></sup> The end came in mid August when the German Army was encircled and trapped in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Falaise_pocket" title="Falaise pocket">Falaise pocket</a>, including the 1 SS <i>Leibstandarte</i>, 10 SS <i>Frundsberg</i> and 12 SS <i>Hitlerjugend</i> and the 17 SS <i>Götz von Berlichingen</i>, while the 2 SS <i>Das Reich</i> and the 9 SS <i>Hohenstaufen</i> were ordered to attack <a href="/wiki/Hill_262" title="Hill 262">Hill 262</a> from the outside in order to keep the gap open.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEJarymowycz2001196_105-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEJarymowycz2001196-105">[104]</a></sup> By 22 August the Falaise pocket had been closed, and all German forces west of the Allied lines were dead or in captivity.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHastings2006306_106-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHastings2006306-106">[105]</a></sup> In the fighting around Hill 262 alone, casualties totalled 2,000 killed and 5,000 taken prisoner.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcGilvray200554_107-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcGilvray200554-107">[106]</a></sup> The 12 SS <i>Hitlerjugend</i> had lost 94 per cent of its armour, nearly all of its artillery, and 70 per cent of its vehicles.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBercuson2004233_108-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBercuson2004233-108">[107]</a></sup> The division had close to 20,000 men and 150 tanks before the campaign started, and was now reduced to 300 men and 10 tanks.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBercuson2004233_108-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBercuson2004233-108">[107]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:German_prisoners_SS-Panzerdivision_Totenkopf.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2480" data-file-width="3312" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/German_prisoners_SS-Panzerdivision_Totenkopf.jpg/220px-German_prisoners_SS-Panzerdivision_Totenkopf.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/German_prisoners_SS-Panzerdivision_Totenkopf.jpg/330px-German_prisoners_SS-Panzerdivision_Totenkopf.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/German_prisoners_SS-Panzerdivision_Totenkopf.jpg/440px-German_prisoners_SS-Panzerdivision_Totenkopf.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:German_prisoners_SS-Panzerdivision_Totenkopf.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Waffen-SS troops taken prisoner in Normandy</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>With the German Army in full retreat, two further Waffen-SS formations entered the battle in France, the <a href="/wiki/SS_Panzergrenadier_Brigade_49" title="SS Panzergrenadier Brigade 49">SS Panzergrenadier Brigade 49</a> and the <a href="/wiki/SS_Panzergrenadier_Brigade_51" title="SS Panzergrenadier Brigade 51">SS Panzergrenadier Brigade 51</a>. Both had been formed in June 1944 from staff and students at the <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/SS-Junkerschule" title="SS-Junkerschule">SS-Junkerschule</a></i>. They were stationed in Denmark to allow the garrison there to move into France, but were brought forward at the beginning of August to the area south and east of Paris. Both Brigades were tasked to hold crossings over the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Seine_River" title="Seine River">Seine River</a> allowing the Army to retreat. Eventually they were forced back and then withdrew, the surviving troops being incorporated into the 17 SS <i>Götz von Berlichingen</i>.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Greece">Greece</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Waffen-SS&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Greece">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>While the bulk of the Waffen-SS was now on the Eastern Front or in Normandy, the 4th SS <i>Polizei</i> Panzergrenadier Division was stationed in <a href="/wiki/Greece" title="Greece">Greece</a> on <a href="/wiki/Internal_security" title="Internal security">internal security</a> duties and anti-partisan operations. On 10 June they committed the <a href="/wiki/Distomo_massacre" title="Distomo massacre">Distomo massacre</a>, when over a period of two hours they went door to door and massacred Greek civilians, reportedly in revenge for a <a href="/wiki/Greek_Resistance" title="Greek Resistance">Greek Resistance</a> attack. In total, 218 men, women and children were killed. According to survivors, the SS forces "<a href="/wiki/Bayonet" title="Bayonet">bayoneted</a> babies in their cribs, stabbed pregnant women, and beheaded the village priest."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBBC_News2003_109-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBBC_News2003-109">[108]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Italy_2">Italy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Waffen-SS&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Italy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>On the Italian Front the 16 SS <i>Reichsführer-SS</i>, conducting anti-partisan operations, is remembered more for the atrocities it perpetrated than its fighting ability: it committed the <a href="/wiki/Sant%27Anna_di_Stazzema_massacre" title="Sant'Anna di Stazzema massacre">Sant'Anna di Stazzema massacre</a> in August 1944<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEJewish_Virtual_Library.2C_Sant.27Anna_massacre_110-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEJewish_Virtual_Library.2C_Sant.27Anna_massacre-110">[109]</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Marzabotto_massacre" title="Marzabotto massacre">Marzabotto massacre</a> between September and October 1944.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBBC_News2007_111-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBBC_News2007-111">[110]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Finland">Finland</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Waffen-SS&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Finland">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>In Finland, the 6 SS <i>Nord</i> had held its lines during the Soviet summer offensive until it was ordered to withdraw from Finland upon the conclusion of an armistice between Finland and the Soviet Union in September 1944. They then formed the rear guard for the three German corps withdrawing from Finland in <a href="/wiki/6th_SS_Mountain_Division_Nord" title="6th SS Mountain Division Nord">Operation Birch</a>, and from September to November 1944 marched 1,600 kilometres to <a href="/wiki/Mo_i_Rana" title="Mo i Rana">Mo i Rana</a>, Norway, where it entrained for the southern end of the country, crossing the <a href="/wiki/Skagerrak" title="Skagerrak">Skagerrak</a> to Denmark.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Arnhem_and_Operation_Market_Garden">Arnhem and Operation Market Garden</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Waffen-SS&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Arnhem and Operation Market Garden">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>In early September 1944, the II SS Panzer Corps (9 SS <i>Hohenstaufen</i> and 10 SS <i>Frundberg</i>) were pulled out of the line and sent to the <a href="/wiki/Arnhem" title="Arnhem">Arnhem</a> area in the Netherlands.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarclerode2005455.E2.80.93456_112-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarclerode2005455.E2.80.93456-112">[111]</a></sup> Upon arrival they began the task of refitting, and the majority of the remaining armoured vehicles were loaded onto trains in preparation for transport to repair depots in Germany. On Sunday 17 September 1944 the Allies launched <a href="/wiki/Operation_Market_Garden" title="Operation Market Garden">Operation Market Garden</a>, and the British <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1st_Airborne_Division" title="1st Airborne Division">1st Airborne Division</a> was dropped in <a href="/wiki/Oosterbeek" title="Oosterbeek">Oosterbeek</a>, to the west of Arnhem. Realizing the threat, <a href="/wiki/Wilhelm_Bittrich" title="Wilhelm Bittrich">Wilhelm Bittrich</a>, commander of II SS Panzer Corps, ordered <i>Hohenstaufen</i> and <i>Frundsberg</i> to ready themselves for combat. Also in the area was the Training and Reserve Battalion, 16th SS Division <i>Reichsführer-SS</i>. The Allied airborne operation was a failure, and <a href="/wiki/Liberation_of_Arnhem" title="Liberation of Arnhem">Arnhem was not liberated</a> until 14 April 1945.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEllis2004313.E2.80.93315_113-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEllis2004313.E2.80.93315-113">[112]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Warsaw_Uprising">Warsaw Uprising</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Waffen-SS&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Warsaw Uprising">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Destroyed_Warsaw,_capital_of_Poland,_January_1945.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="824" data-file-width="1000" height="181" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Destroyed_Warsaw%2C_capital_of_Poland%2C_January_1945.jpg/220px-Destroyed_Warsaw%2C_capital_of_Poland%2C_January_1945.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Destroyed_Warsaw%2C_capital_of_Poland%2C_January_1945.jpg/330px-Destroyed_Warsaw%2C_capital_of_Poland%2C_January_1945.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Destroyed_Warsaw%2C_capital_of_Poland%2C_January_1945.jpg/440px-Destroyed_Warsaw%2C_capital_of_Poland%2C_January_1945.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Destroyed_Warsaw,_capital_of_Poland,_January_1945.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Ruins of Warsaw's <a href="/wiki/Old_Town_Market_Place,_Warsaw" title="Old Town Market Place, Warsaw">old town market square</a>. In total, eighty-five percent of the city <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Aftereffects_of_the_Warsaw_Uprising" title="Aftereffects of the Warsaw Uprising">was destroyed</a> and nearly 200,000 civilians killed.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>At the other end of Europe, the Waffen-SS was dealing with the <a href="/wiki/Warsaw_Uprising" title="Warsaw Uprising">Warsaw Uprising</a>. Between August and October 1944, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dirlewanger_Brigade" title="Dirlewanger Brigade">Dirlewanger Brigade</a> (recruited from criminals and the mentally ill throughout Germany) and the <a href="/wiki/S.S._Sturmbrigade_R.O.N.A." title="S.S. Sturmbrigade R.O.N.A.">S.S. Sturmbrigade R.O.N.A.</a> <i>Russkaya Osvoboditelnaya Narodnaya Armiya (Russian National Liberation Army)</i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114"><a href="#cite_note-114">[113]</a></sup> which was made up of ethnic Russian collaborators were both sent to <a href="/wiki/Warsaw" title="Warsaw">Warsaw</a> to put down the uprising. During the battle, the <i>Dirlewanger</i> behaved atrociously, raping, looting, and killing citizens of Warsaw regardless of whether they belonged to the Polish resistance or not; the unit commander <a href="/wiki/Oskar_Dirlewanger" title="Oskar Dirlewanger">SS-<i>Oberführer</i> Oskar Dirlewanger</a> encouraged their excesses. The unit's behavior was reportedly so bestial and indiscriminate that Himmler was forced to send a battalion of SS military police to ensure the Dirlewanger convicts did not turn their aggressions against the leadership of the brigade or other nearby German units.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBell196689.E2.80.9391_115-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBell196689.E2.80.9391-115">[114]</a></sup> At the same time they were encouraged by Himmler to terrorize freely, take no prisoners, and generally indulge their perverse tendencies. Favoured tactics of the Dirlewanger men during the siege reportedly included the ubiquitous gang rape of female Poles, both women and children; playing "bayonet catch" with live babies; and torturing captives to death by hacking off their arms, dousing them with gasoline, and setting them alight to run armless and flaming down the street.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEConot1984278.E2.80.93281_116-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEConot1984278.E2.80.93281-116">[115]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBell196689.E2.80.9391_115-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBell196689.E2.80.9391-115">[114]</a></sup> The Dirlewanger brigade committed almost non-stop atrocities during this period, in particular the four-day <a href="/wiki/Wola_massacre" title="Wola massacre">Wola massacre</a>.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Polish_civilians_murdered_by_German-SS-troops_in_Warsaw_Uprising_Warsaw_August_1944.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="336" data-file-width="400" height="185" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Polish_civilians_murdered_by_German-SS-troops_in_Warsaw_Uprising_Warsaw_August_1944.jpg/220px-Polish_civilians_murdered_by_German-SS-troops_in_Warsaw_Uprising_Warsaw_August_1944.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Polish_civilians_murdered_by_German-SS-troops_in_Warsaw_Uprising_Warsaw_August_1944.jpg/330px-Polish_civilians_murdered_by_German-SS-troops_in_Warsaw_Uprising_Warsaw_August_1944.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/6/66/Polish_civilians_murdered_by_German-SS-troops_in_Warsaw_Uprising_Warsaw_August_1944.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Polish_civilians_murdered_by_German-SS-troops_in_Warsaw_Uprising_Warsaw_August_1944.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Photo taken by the <a href="/wiki/Polish_resistance_movement_in_World_War_II" title="Polish resistance movement in World War II">Polish Underground</a> showing the bodies of women and children murdered by SS troops in Warsaw Uprising, August 1944</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The other unit, <i>Waffen-Sturm-Brigade R.O.N.A.</i> was tasked with clearing the <a href="/wiki/Ochota" title="Ochota">Ochota</a> district in Warsaw that was defended by members of the Polish <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Armia_Krajowa" title="Armia Krajowa">Home Army</a>. Their attack was planned for the morning of 5 August, but when the time came, the RONA unit could not be found; after some searching by the SS military police, members of the unit were found looting abandoned houses in the rear of the German column. Later, thousands of Polish civilians were killed by the RONA SS men during the events known as <a href="/wiki/Ochota_massacre" title="Ochota massacre">Ochota massacre</a>; many victims were also raped.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117"><a href="#cite_note-117">[b]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118"><a href="#cite_note-118">[c]</a></sup> In following weeks, the RONA unit was moved south to the <a href="/wiki/Wola" title="Wola">Wola</a> district, but it fared no better in combat there than it did in Ochota; in one incident a sub-unit of the RONA brigade advanced to loot a captured building on the <a href="/wiki/Front_line" title="Front line">front line</a>, but was subsequently cut off from the rest of the SS formation and wiped out by the Poles. Following the fiasco, <a href="/wiki/Bronislav_Kaminski" title="Bronislav Kaminski">SS-Brigadeführer Bronislav Vladislavovich Kaminski</a>, the unit's commander, was called to <a href="/wiki/%C5%81%C3%B3d%C5%BA" title="Łódź">Łódź</a> to attend a SS leadership conference. He never arrived; official Nazi sources blamed Polish partisans for an alleged ambush that killed the RONA commander. But according to various other sources he was arrested and tried by the SS, or simply shot on the spot by the <a href="/wiki/Gestapo" title="Gestapo">Gestapo</a>. The behaviour of the <i>RONA</i> during the battle was an embarrassment even to the SS, and the alleged rape and murder of two German <a href="/wiki/Strength_Through_Joy" title="Strength Through Joy">Strength Through Joy</a> girls may have played a part in the eventual execution of the brigade's commander.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKirchmayer1978367_119-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKirchmayer1978367-119">[116]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Vistula_River_line">Vistula River line</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Waffen-SS&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Vistula River line">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>In late August 1944, 5 SS <i>Wiking</i> was ordered back to <a href="/wiki/Modlin_(Nowy_Dw%C3%B3r_Mazowiecki)" title="Modlin (Nowy Dwór Mazowiecki)">Modlin</a> on the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vistula_River" title="Vistula River">Vistula River</a> line near Warsaw, where it was to join the newly formed <a href="/wiki/Army_Group_Vistula" title="Army Group Vistula">Army Group Vistula</a>. Fighting alongside the Luftwaffe's <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fallschirm-Panzer_Division_1_Hermann_G%C3%B6ring" title="Fallschirm-Panzer Division 1 Hermann Göring">Fallschirm-Panzer Division 1 <i>Hermann Göring</i></a>, they annihilated the Soviet 3rd Tank Corps. The advent of the Warsaw Uprising brought the Soviet offensive to a halt, and relative peace fell on the front line. The division remained in the Modlin area for the rest of the year, grouped with the 3 SS <i>Totenkopf</i> in the <a href="/wiki/IV_SS_Panzer_Corps" title="IV SS Panzer Corps">IV SS Panzer Corps</a>. Heavy defensive battles around Modlin followed for the rest of the year. Together they helped force the Red Army out of Warsaw and back across the Vistula River<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Accuracy_dispute#Disputed_statement" title="Wikipedia:Accuracy dispute"><span title="The material near this tag is possibly inaccurate or nonfactual. (December 2016)">dubious</span></a> <span class="metadata">– <a href="/wiki/Talk:Waffen-SS#Dubious" title="Talk:Waffen-SS">discuss</a></span></i>]</sup>, where the Front stabilized until January 1945.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Ardennes_Offensive">Ardennes Offensive</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Waffen-SS&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Ardennes Offensive">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Kampfgruppe_Knittel%27s_troops_on_the_road_to_Stavelot.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="466" data-file-width="648" height="158" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Kampfgruppe_Knittel%27s_troops_on_the_road_to_Stavelot.jpg/220px-Kampfgruppe_Knittel%27s_troops_on_the_road_to_Stavelot.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Kampfgruppe_Knittel%27s_troops_on_the_road_to_Stavelot.jpg/330px-Kampfgruppe_Knittel%27s_troops_on_the_road_to_Stavelot.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Kampfgruppe_Knittel%27s_troops_on_the_road_to_Stavelot.jpg/440px-Kampfgruppe_Knittel%27s_troops_on_the_road_to_Stavelot.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Kampfgruppe_Knittel%27s_troops_on_the_road_to_Stavelot.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Kampfgruppe <a href="/wiki/Gustav_Knittel" title="Gustav Knittel">Knittel</a>'s troops on the road to <a href="/wiki/Stavelot" title="Stavelot">Stavelot</a> to support Peiper</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_the_Bulge" title="Battle of the Bulge">Ardennes Offensive</a> or "Battle of the Bulge", between 16 December 1944 and 25 January 1945, was a major German offensive through the forested <a href="/wiki/Ardennes" title="Ardennes">Ardennes Mountains region</a> of Belgium. The Waffen-SS units included the <a href="/wiki/6th_Panzer_Army" title="6th Panzer Army">6th Panzer Army</a> under <a href="/wiki/Sepp_Dietrich" title="Sepp Dietrich">Sepp Dietrich</a>. Created on 26 October 1944, it incorporated the <a href="/wiki/I_SS_Panzer_Corps" title="I SS Panzer Corps">I SS Panzer Corps</a> (1 SS <i>Leibstandarte</i>, the 12 SS <i>Hitlerjugend</i> and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/SS_Heavy_Panzer_Battalion_101" title="SS Heavy Panzer Battalion 101">SS Heavy Panzer Battalion 101</a>). It also had the <a href="/wiki/II_SS_Panzer_Corps" title="II SS Panzer Corps">II SS Panzer Corps</a> (2 SS <i>Das Reich</i> and the 9 SS <i>Hohenstaufen</i>). Another unit involved was <a href="/wiki/Otto_Skorzeny" title="Otto Skorzeny">Otto Skorzeny</a>'s <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/SS_Panzer_Brigade_150" title="SS Panzer Brigade 150">SS Panzer Brigade 150</a>.</p>
<p>The purpose of the attack was to split the British and American line in half, capture <a href="/wiki/Antwerp" title="Antwerp">Antwerp</a>, and encircle and destroy four Allied armies, forcing the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Western_Allies" title="Western Allies">Western Allies</a> to negotiate a <a href="/wiki/Peace_treaty" title="Peace treaty">peace treaty</a> on terms favorable to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Axis_powers_of_World_War_II" title="Axis powers of World War II">Axis Powers</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEUnited_States_History_120-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEUnited_States_History-120">[117]</a></sup> However, advancing through the forests and wooded hills of the Ardennes proved difficult in the winter weather. Initially the Germans made good progress in the northern end of its advance. However, they ran into unexpectedly strong resistance by the U.S. 2nd and 99th Infantry Divisions. By 23 December, weather conditions started improving, allowing the Allied air forces, which had been grounded, to attack. In increasingly difficult conditions, the German advance slowed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWeinberg1994767_121-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWeinberg1994767-121">[118]</a></sup> The attack was ultimately a failure. Despite the efforts of the Waffen-SS and the German Army, the fuel shortages, stiff American resistance, including in and around the town of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Battle_of_Bastogne" title="Battle of Bastogne">Bastogne</a> and Allied air-assaults on German supply columns proved too much, costing the Germans 700 tanks and most of their remaining mobile forces in the west.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWeinberg1994767.E2.80.93769_122-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWeinberg1994767.E2.80.93769-122">[119]</a></sup> Hitler's failed counteroffensive had used most of Germany's remaining reserves of manpower and materiel, which could not be replaced.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEStein1984232_123-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEStein1984232-123">[120]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Malmedy_Massacre.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1004" data-file-width="1476" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Malmedy_Massacre.jpg/220px-Malmedy_Massacre.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Malmedy_Massacre.jpg/330px-Malmedy_Massacre.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Malmedy_Massacre.jpg/440px-Malmedy_Massacre.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Malmedy_Massacre.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Aftermath of the Malmedy Massacre</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>During the battle, <i>Kampfgruppe</i> Peiper, part of the 1 SS <i>Leibstandarte</i>, left a path of destruction, which included Waffen-SS men murdering American POWs and unarmed Belgian civilians.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMurrayMillett2001468_124-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMurrayMillett2001468-124">[121]</a></sup> It is infamous for the <a href="/wiki/Malmedy_massacre" title="Malmedy massacre">Malmedy massacre</a>, in which approximately 90 unarmed American <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/POW" title="POW">prisoners of war</a> were murdered on 17 December 1944.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEReynolds2003_125-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEReynolds2003-125">[122]</a></sup> Also during this battle, 3./SS-PzAA1 LSSAH captured and shot eleven African-American soldiers from the American <a href="/wiki/333rd_Field_Artillery_Battalion_(United_States)" title="333rd Field Artillery Battalion (United States)">333rd Artillery Battalion</a> in the hamlet of Wereth. Their remains were found by Allied troops two months later. The soldiers had their fingers cut off and legs broken, and one was shot while trying to bandage a comrade's wounds.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEUS_Memorial_Wereth_126-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEUS_Memorial_Wereth-126">[123]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Siege_of_Budapest">Siege of Budapest</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Waffen-SS&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Siege of Budapest">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>In late December 1944, the Axis forces, including IX Waffen Mountain Corps of the SS (Croatian), defending <a href="/wiki/Budapest" title="Budapest">Budapest</a>, were encircled in the <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Budapest" title="Siege of Budapest">Siege of Budapest</a>. The IV SS Panzer Corps (3 SS <i>Totenkopf</i> and 5 SS <i>Wiking</i>) was ordered south to join <a href="/wiki/Hermann_Balck" title="Hermann Balck">Hermann Balck</a>'s <a href="/wiki/6th_Army_(Wehrmacht)" title="6th Army (Wehrmacht)">6th Army</a> (Army Group <i>Balck</i>), which was mustering for a relief effort code named <a href="/wiki/Operation_Konrad" title="Operation Konrad">Operation Konrad</a>.</p>
<p>As a part of Operation Konrad I, the IV SS Panzer Corps was committed to action on 1 January 1945, near <a href="/wiki/Tata,_Hungary" title="Tata, Hungary">Tata</a>, with the advance columns of <i>Wiking</i> slamming into the Soviet <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/4th_Guards_Army_(Soviet_Union)" title="4th Guards Army (Soviet Union)">4th Guards Army</a>. A heavy battle ensued, with the 5 SS <i>Wiking</i> and 3 SS <i>Totenkopf</i> destroying many of the Soviet tanks. In three days their panzer spearheads had driven 45 kilometres, over half the distance from the start point to Budapest. The Red Army maneuvered forces to block the advance, halting them at <a href="/wiki/Bicske" title="Bicske">Bicske</a>, 28 kilometres (17 mi) from Budapest. Two further attacks, Operations Konrad II and III, also failed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEZwack1999_127-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEZwack1999-127">[124]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hungarian_Third_Army" title="Hungarian Third Army">Hungarian Third Army</a> was besieged in Budapest along with the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/IX_Waffen_Mountain_Corps_of_the_SS_(Croatian)" title="IX Waffen Mountain Corps of the SS (Croatian)">IX Waffen Mountain Corps of the SS (Croatian)</a> (8 SS <i>Florian Geyer</i> and 22 SS <i>Maria Theresia</i>). The siege lasted from 29 December 1944 until the city surrendered unconditionally on 13 February 1945. Only 170 men of the 22 SS <i>Maria Theresia</i> made it back to the German lines.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1945">1945</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Waffen-SS&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: 1945">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="1945_expansion">1945 expansion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Waffen-SS&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: 1945 expansion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The Waffen-SS continued to expand in 1945. January saw the <a href="/wiki/32nd_SS_Volunteer_Grenadier_Division_30_Januar" title="32nd SS Volunteer Grenadier Division 30 Januar">32nd SS Volunteer Grenadier Division <i>30 Januar</i></a> formed from the remnants of other units and staff from the SS-Junkerschules. In February the Waffen-Grenadier-Brigade der SS "Charlemagne" was upgraded to a division and became known as the <a href="/wiki/33rd_Waffen_Grenadier_Division_of_the_SS_Charlemagne_(1st_French)" title="33rd Waffen Grenadier Division of the SS Charlemagne (1st French)">33rd Waffen Grenadier Division of the SS <i>Charlemagne</i> (1st French)</a>. At this time it had a strength of 7,340 men.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELittlejohn1987170.2C_172_128-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELittlejohn1987170.2C_172-128">[125]</a></sup> The SS Volunteer Grenadier-Brigade Landstorm Nederland was upgraded to the <a href="/wiki/34th_SS_Volunteer_Grenadier_Division_Landstorm_Nederland" title="34th SS Volunteer Grenadier Division Landstorm Nederland">34th SS Volunteer Grenadier Division <i>Landstorm Nederland</i></a>. The second SS Police division followed when the <a href="/wiki/35th_SS_and_Police_Grenadier_Division" title="35th SS and Police Grenadier Division">35th SS and Police Grenadier Division</a> was formed from SS Police units that had been transferred to the Waffen-SS. The Dirlewanger Brigade was reformed as the <a href="/wiki/36th_Waffen_Grenadier_Division_of_the_SS" title="36th Waffen Grenadier Division of the SS">36th Waffen Grenadier Division of the SS</a>. There was now a real shortage of Waffen-SS volunteers and conscripts, so units from the Army were attached to bring it up to strength. The third SS Cavalry division <a href="/wiki/37th_SS_Volunteer_Cavalry_Division_L%C3%BCtzow" title="37th SS Volunteer Cavalry Division Lützow">37th SS Volunteer Cavalry Division <i>Lützow</i></a> was formed from the remnants of the 8 SS <i>Florian Geyer</i> and 22 SS <i>Maria Theresia</i>, which had both been virtually destroyed. The last Waffen-SS division was the <a href="/wiki/38th_SS_Division_Nibelungen" title="38th SS Division Nibelungen">38th SS Division <i>Nibelungen</i></a>, which was also formed from students and staff from the SS-Junkerschule, but consisted of only around 6,000 men, the strength of a normal brigade.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/XV_SS_Cossack_Cavalry_Corps" title="XV SS Cossack Cavalry Corps">XV SS Cossack Cavalry Corps</a>, which contained the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1st_Cossack_Division" title="1st Cossack Division">1 SS Cossack Division</a>, was transferred to the Waffen-SS on 1 February 1945. Despite the refusal of its commander, General von Pannwitz, to enter the SS, the corps was placed under SS administration and all Cossacks became formally part of the Waffen-SS.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMichaelis200636_129-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMichaelis200636-129">[126]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Operation_Nordwind">Operation Nordwind</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Waffen-SS&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Operation Nordwind">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p><a href="/wiki/Operation_Nordwind" title="Operation Nordwind">Operation Nordwind</a> was the last major German offensive on the Western Front. It began on 1 January 1945 in <a href="/wiki/Alsace" title="Alsace">Alsace</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lorraine_(province)" title="Lorraine (province)">Lorraine</a> in north-eastern France, and it ended on 25 January. The initial attack was conducted by three Corps of the 1st Army. By 15 January at least 17 German divisions (including units in the <a href="/wiki/Colmar_Pocket" title="Colmar Pocket">Colmar Pocket</a>) were engaged, including the <a href="/wiki/XIII_SS_Army_Corps" title="XIII SS Army Corps">XIII SS Army Corps</a> (17 SS <i>Götz von Berlichingen</i> and 38 SS <i>Nibelungen</i>) and the 6 SS <i>Nord</i> and 10 SS <i>Frundsberg</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTE100th_Division_130-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTE100th_Division-130">[127]</a></sup> At the same time, the Luftwaffe mounted a large offensive over the skies of France. Some 240 fighters were lost and just as many pilots. It was the 'last gasp' attempt for the Luftwaffe to take back air supremacy from the western allies.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Operation_Solstice">Operation Solstice</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Waffen-SS&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Operation Solstice">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p><a href="/wiki/Operation_Solstice" title="Operation Solstice">Operation Solstice</a>, or the "Stargard Tank Battle" (February 1945) was one of the last <a href="/wiki/Armoured_warfare" title="Armoured warfare">armoured</a> offensive operations on the Eastern Front. It was a limited counter-attack by the three Corps of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eleventh_SS_Panzer_Army" title="Eleventh SS Panzer Army">Eleventh SS Panzer Army</a>, which was being assembled in <a href="/wiki/Pomerania" title="Pomerania">Pomerania</a>, against the spearheads of the 1st Belorussian Front. Originally planned as a major offensive, it was executed as a more limited attack. It was repulsed by the Red Army, but helped to convince the <a href="/wiki/Stavka" title="Stavka">Soviet High Command</a> to postpone the planned attack on <a href="/wiki/Berlin" title="Berlin">Berlin</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBeevor200291_131-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBeevor200291-131">[128]</a></sup></p>
<p>Initially the attack achieved a total surprise, reaching the banks of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ina_River" title="Ina River">Ina River</a> and, on 17 January, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arnswalde" title="Arnswalde">Arnswalde</a>. Strong Soviet counter-attacks halted the advance, and the operation was called off. The III (Germanic) SS Panzer Corps, was pulled back to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Stargard_Szczeci%C5%84ski" title="Stargard Szczeciński">Stargard</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Stettin" title="Stettin">Stettin</a> on the northern <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Oder_River" title="Oder River">Oder River</a>.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="East_Pomeranian_Offensive">East Pomeranian Offensive</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Waffen-SS&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: East Pomeranian Offensive">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/East_Pomeranian_Offensive" title="East Pomeranian Offensive">East Pomeranian Offensive</a> lasted from 24 February to 4 April, in <a href="/wiki/Pomerania" title="Pomerania">Pomerania</a> and <a href="/wiki/West_Prussia" title="West Prussia">West Prussia</a>. The Waffen-SS units involved were the 11 SS <i>Nordland</i>, 20 SS <i>Estonian</i>, 23 SS <i>Nederland</i>, 27 SS <i>Langemark</i>, 28 SS <i>Wallonien</i>, all in the <a href="/wiki/III_(Germanic)_SS_Panzer_Corps" title="III (Germanic) SS Panzer Corps">III (Germanic) SS Panzer Corps</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/X_SS_Corps" title="X SS Corps">X SS Corps</a>, which did not command any SS units.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERaus2005324.E2.80.93332_132-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERaus2005324.E2.80.93332-132">[129]</a></sup></p>
<p>In March 1945, the X SS Corps was encircled by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Soviet_1st_Guards_Tank_Army" title="Soviet 1st Guards Tank Army">1st Guards Tank Army</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/3rd_Shock_Army_(Soviet_Union)" title="3rd Shock Army (Soviet Union)">3rd Shock Army</a>, and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/First_Polish_Army_(1944%E2%80%931945)" title="First Polish Army (1944–1945)">Polish 1st Army</a> in the area of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dramburg" title="Dramburg">Dramburg</a>. This pocket was destroyed by the Red Army on 7 March 1945.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETessin1973164_133-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETessin1973164-133">[130]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEUstinow1981179_134-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEUstinow1981179-134">[131]</a></sup> On 8 March 1945, the Soviet forces announced the capture of General Krappe and 8,000 men of the X SS Corps.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESchramm19821156_135-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESchramm19821156-135">[132]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Operation_Spring_Awakening">Operation Spring Awakening</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Waffen-SS&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Operation Spring Awakening">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_Bild_146-1989-105-13A,_Ungarn,_deutscher_R%C3%BCckzug.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="567" data-file-width="800" height="156" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Bundesarchiv_Bild_146-1989-105-13A%2C_Ungarn%2C_deutscher_R%C3%BCckzug.jpg/220px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_146-1989-105-13A%2C_Ungarn%2C_deutscher_R%C3%BCckzug.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Bundesarchiv_Bild_146-1989-105-13A%2C_Ungarn%2C_deutscher_R%C3%BCckzug.jpg/330px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_146-1989-105-13A%2C_Ungarn%2C_deutscher_R%C3%BCckzug.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Bundesarchiv_Bild_146-1989-105-13A%2C_Ungarn%2C_deutscher_R%C3%BCckzug.jpg/440px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_146-1989-105-13A%2C_Ungarn%2C_deutscher_R%C3%BCckzug.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_Bild_146-1989-105-13A,_Ungarn,_deutscher_R%C3%BCckzug.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
German units during the Lake Balaton Offensive, March 1945</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>After the Ardennes offensive failed, in Hitler’s estimation, the Nagykanizsa oilfields southwest of <a href="/wiki/Lake_Balaton" title="Lake Balaton">Lake Balaton</a> were the most strategically valuable reserves on the Eastern Front.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDuffy2002293_136-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDuffy2002293-136">[133]</a></sup> The SS Divisions were pulled out and refitted in Germany in preparation for <a href="/wiki/Operation_Spring_Awakening" title="Operation Spring Awakening">Operation Spring Awakening</a> (<i>Frühlingserwachsen</i>). Hitler ordered Dietrich’s 6th SS Panzer Army to take the lead and move to Hungary in order to protect the oilfields and refineries there.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESeaton1971537_137-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESeaton1971537-137">[134]</a></sup> The 6th SS Panzer Army was made up of the I SS Panzer Corps (1 SS <i>Leibstandarte</i> and 12 SS <i>Hitlerjugend</i>) and the II SS Panzer Corps (2 SS <i>Das Reich</i> and the 10 SS <i>Frundsberg</i>). Also present but not part of the 6th SS Panzer Army was the IV SS Panzer Corps (3 SS <i>Totenkopf</i> and 5 SS <i>Wiking</i>).</p>
<p>This final German offensive in the east began on 6 March. The German forces attacked near Lake Balaton with the Sixth SS Panzer Army advancing northwards towards Budapest and the 2nd Panzer Army moving eastwards and south.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDuffy2002294_138-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDuffy2002294-138">[135]</a></sup> Dietrich's army made "good progress" at first, but as they drew near the Danube, the combination of the muddy terrain and strong resistance of the Soviet forces ground them to a halt.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEStein1984238_139-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEStein1984238-139">[136]</a></sup> The overwhelming numerical superiority of the Red Army made any defense impossible, yet Hitler somehow had believed victory was attainable.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEZiemke1968450_140-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEZiemke1968450-140">[137]</a></sup></p>
<p>After Operation Spring Awakening, the 6th SS Panzer Army withdrew towards <a href="/wiki/Vienna" title="Vienna">Vienna</a> and was involved what became known as the <a href="/wiki/Vienna_Offensive" title="Vienna Offensive">Vienna Offensive</a>. The only major force to face the attacking Red Army was the II SS Panzer Corps (2 SS <i>Das Reich</i> and 3 SS <i>Totenkopf</i>), under the command of <a href="/wiki/Wilhelm_Bittrich" title="Wilhelm Bittrich">Wilhelm Bittrich</a>, along with <i>ad hoc</i> forces made up of garrison and anti-aircraft units. Vienna fell to the Soviet forces on 13 April.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEUstinow1981238.E2.80.93239_141-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEUstinow1981238.E2.80.93239-141">[138]</a></sup> Bittrich's II SS Panzer Corps had pulled out to the west that evening to avoid encirclement.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGosztony1978262_142-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGosztony1978262-142">[139]</a></sup> The LSSAH retreated westward with less than 1,600 men and 16 tanks remaining.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcNab2013280_143-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcNab2013280-143">[140]</a></sup></p>
<p>This failure is famous for the "armband order" that followed. The order was issued to the Sixth SS Panzer Army commander Sepp Dietrich by Adolf Hitler, who claimed that the troops, and more importantly, the 1 SS <i>Leibstandarte</i>, "did not fight as the situation demanded."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDollinger1967198_144-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDollinger1967198-144">[141]</a></sup> As a mark of disgrace, the Waffen-SS units involved in the battle were ordered to remove their distinctive <a href="/wiki/Cuff_title" title="Cuff title">cuff titles</a>. Dietrich did not relay the order to his troops.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEStein1984238_139-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEStein1984238-139">[136]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Berlin">Berlin</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Waffen-SS&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Berlin">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Army_Group_Vistula" title="Army Group Vistula">Army Group Vistula</a> was formed in 1945 to protect Berlin from the advancing Red Army. It fought in the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_the_Seelow_Heights" title="Battle of the Seelow Heights">Battle of the Seelow Heights</a> (16–19 April) and the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Halbe" title="Battle of Halbe">Battle of Halbe</a> (21 April – 1 May), both part of the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Berlin" title="Battle of Berlin">Battle of Berlin</a>. The Waffen-SS was represented by the III (Germanic) SS Panzer Corps.</p>
<p>On 23 April, <i>Brigadeführer</i> <a href="/wiki/Wilhelm_Mohnke" title="Wilhelm Mohnke">Wilhelm Mohnke</a> was appointed by Hitler as Battle Commander for the centre government district (Zitadelle sector), which included the <a href="/wiki/Reich_Chancellery" title="Reich Chancellery">Reich Chancellery</a> and <i><a href="/wiki/F%C3%BChrerbunker" title="Führerbunker">Führerbunker</a></i>. Mohnke's command post was in the bunkers under the Reich Chancellery.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFischer200842.E2.80.9343_145-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFischer200842.E2.80.9343-145">[142]</a></sup> He formed <i>Kampfgruppe Mohnke</i> (Battle Group Mohnke), divided into two weak regiments. It was made up of the LSSAH Flak Company, replacements from LSSAH Training and Reserve Battalion from Spreenhagan (under <i>Standartenfuhrer</i> Anhalt),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFischer200842.E2.80.9343_145-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFischer200842.E2.80.9343-145">[142]</a></sup> 600 men from the <i><a href="/wiki/Begleit-Bataillon_Reichsf%C3%BChrer-SS" title="Begleit-Bataillon Reichsführer-SS">Begleit-Bataillon Reichsführer-SS</a></i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEStein1984162_146-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEStein1984162-146">[143]</a></sup> the Führer-Begleit-Company, and the core group—800 men of the LSSAH Guard Battalion assigned to guard the Führer.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFischer200842.E2.80.9343_145-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFischer200842.E2.80.9343-145">[142]</a></sup></p>
