<p>The <a href="/wiki/Reich_Chancellery" title="Reich Chancellery">Reich Chancellery</a> on 23 April ordered <i>Brigadeführer</i> <a href="/wiki/Gustav_Krukenberg" title="Gustav Krukenberg">Gustav Krukenberg</a> to proceed to the capital with his men, who were reorganized as <i>Sturmbataillon</i> ("assault battalion") "Charlemagne". Between 320 and 330 French troops arrived in Berlin on 24 April after a long detour to avoid Soviet advance columns.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEForbes2010396.E2.80.93398_147-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEForbes2010396.E2.80.93398-147">[144]</a></sup> Krukenberg was also appointed the commander of (Berlin) Defence Sector C. This included the <i>Nordland</i> Division, whose previous commander, <a href="/wiki/Joachim_Ziegler" title="Joachim Ziegler">Joachim Ziegler</a>, was relieved of his command the same day.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBeevor2002301_148-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBeevor2002301-148">[145]</a></sup> On 27 April, after a futile defence, the remnants of <i>Nordland</i> were pushed back into the centre government district (Zitadelle sector) in Defence sector Z. There Krukenberg's <i>Nordland</i> headquarters was a carriage in the Stadtmitte U-Bahn station.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBeevor2002323_149-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBeevor2002323-149">[146]</a></sup> The men of <i>Nordland</i> were now under Mohnke's overall command. Among the men were French, Latvian, and Scandinavian Waffen-SS troops.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEStein1984246_150-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEStein1984246-150">[147]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcNab2013328.2C_330.2C_338_151-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcNab2013328.2C_330.2C_338-151">[148]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:207px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-R77767,_Berlin,_Rotarmisten_Unter_den_Linden.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="500" data-file-width="801" height="128" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-R77767%2C_Berlin%2C_Rotarmisten_Unter_den_Linden.jpg/205px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-R77767%2C_Berlin%2C_Rotarmisten_Unter_den_Linden.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-R77767%2C_Berlin%2C_Rotarmisten_Unter_den_Linden.jpg/308px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-R77767%2C_Berlin%2C_Rotarmisten_Unter_den_Linden.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-R77767%2C_Berlin%2C_Rotarmisten_Unter_den_Linden.jpg/410px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-R77767%2C_Berlin%2C_Rotarmisten_Unter_den_Linden.jpg 2x" width="205"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-R77767,_Berlin,_Rotarmisten_Unter_den_Linden.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
After the battle, Soviet soldiers hoist the Soviet flag on the balcony of the <a href="/wiki/Hotel_Adlon" title="Hotel Adlon">Hotel Adlon</a> in Berlin</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Heavy artillery bombardment of the centre government district had begun on 20 April 1945 and lasted until the end of hostilities. Under the intense shelling, the SS troops put up stiff resistance which led to bitter and bloody street fighting with the Soviet Red Army forces.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBeevor2002365.E2.80.93367.2C_372_152-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBeevor2002365.E2.80.93367.2C_372-152">[149]</a></sup> By 26 April, the <i>Nordland</i> defenders were pushed back into the Reichstag and Reich Chancellery. There over the next few days, the survivors (mainly French SS troops from the former 33 SS <i>Charlemagne</i>) fought in vain against the Soviet army forces.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWeale2012407_153-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWeale2012407-153">[150]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Himmler_Dead.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="800" data-file-width="799" height="170" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Himmler_Dead.jpg/170px-Himmler_Dead.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Himmler_Dead.jpg/255px-Himmler_Dead.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Himmler_Dead.jpg/340px-Himmler_Dead.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Himmler_Dead.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Himmler's corpse after his suicide, May 1945</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>On 30 April, after receiving news of Hitler's suicide, orders were issued that those who could do so were to break out. Prior to the breakout Mohnke briefed all commanders that could be reached within the Zitadelle sector about Hitler's death and the planned breakout.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFischer200849_154-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFischer200849-154">[151]</a></sup> The break out started at 2300 hours on 1 May. There were ten main groups that attempted to head northwest towards Mecklenburg. Fierce fighting continued all around, especially in the <a href="/wiki/Weidendammer_Bridge" title="Weidendammer Bridge">Weidendammer Bridge</a> area. What was left of the 11 SS <i>Nordland</i> under <i>Brigadeführer</i> Krukenberg fought hard in that area, but the Soviet artillery, anti-tank guns and tanks destroyed the groups. Several very small groups managed to reach the Americans at the <a href="/wiki/Elbe" title="Elbe">Elbe</a>'s west bank, but most, including Mohnke's group, could not make it through the Soviet rings.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFischer200849_154-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFischer200849-154">[151]</a></sup></p>
<p>As for <i><a href="/wiki/Reichsf%C3%BChrer-SS" title="Reichsführer-SS">Reichsführer-SS</a></i> Himmler, he attempted to go into hiding. Using a forged paybook under the name of Sergeant Heinrich Hitzinger, he fled south on 11 May to <a href="/wiki/Friedrichskoog" title="Friedrichskoog">Friedrichskoog</a>. On 21 May, Himmler and two aides were detained at a checkpoint set up by former Soviet POWs and then handed over to the British Army. On 23 May, after admitting his real identity, a doctor attempted to examine him. However, Himmler bit into a hidden cyanide pill and collapsed onto the floor. He was dead within 15 minutes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTE.27.27Bend_Bulletin.27.271945_155-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTE.27.27Bend_Bulletin.27.271945-155">[152]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELongerich20121.E2.80.933_156-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELongerich20121.E2.80.933-156">[153]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Commanders">Commanders</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Waffen-SS&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: Commanders">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Sepp_Dietrich" title="Sepp Dietrich">Josef "Sepp" Dietrich</a> was a former Army sergeant with a <a href="/wiki/Peasant" title="Peasant">peasant</a> background who commanded the forerunner of the Waffen-SS, the Sonderkommando Berlin. He would command the <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1_SS" title="1 SS">Leibstandarte SS Adolf Hitler</a></i> from its inception to <a href="/wiki/Regiment" title="Regiment">regiment</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brigade" title="Brigade">brigade</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Military_division" title="Military division">division</a>. He was then given command of the <a href="/wiki/I_SS_Panzer_Corps" title="I SS Panzer Corps">I SS Panzer Corps</a> and by the end of the war was the commander of the <a href="/wiki/6th_Panzer_Army" title="6th Panzer Army">6th SS Panzer Army</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFlaherty2004144_11-5"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFlaherty2004144-11">[11]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Paul_Hausser" title="Paul Hausser">Paul Hausser</a>, a former general in the regular army, was chosen by Himmler to transform the SS-VT into a credible military organisation. He was the first divisional commander of the Waffen-SS when the SS-VT was formed into a division for the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_France" title="Battle of France">Battle of France</a>. He went on to command the <a href="/wiki/II_SS_Panzer_Corps" title="II SS Panzer Corps">II SS Panzer Corps</a> and the <a href="/wiki/7th_Army_(Wehrmacht)" title="7th Army (Wehrmacht)">7th Army</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFlaherty2004146_21-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFlaherty2004146-21">[21]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Artur_Phleps" title="Artur Phleps">Artur Phleps</a>, a former <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Romania" title="Kingdom of Romania">Romanian</a> general who joined the Waffen-SS, raised and commanded the <a href="/wiki/7th_SS_Volunteer_Mountain_Division_Prinz_Eugen" title="7th SS Volunteer Mountain Division Prinz Eugen">7th SS Volunteer Mountain Division <i>Prinz Eugen</i></a> then rose to command the <a href="/wiki/V_SS_Mountain_Corps" title="V SS Mountain Corps">V SS Mountain Corps</a> which fought the <a href="/wiki/Yugoslav_Partisans" title="Yugoslav Partisans">Yugoslav Partisans</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEStein1984210_157-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEStein1984210-157">[154]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Felix_Steiner" title="Felix Steiner">Felix Steiner</a>, another former army officer and veteran of <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a>. He was given command of the SS Regiment <i>Deutschland</i>. He is credited with the creation of small mobile <a href="/wiki/Battlegroup_(army)" title="Battlegroup (army)">battle groups</a>. He armed his men with <a href="/wiki/Submachine_gun" title="Submachine gun">submachine guns</a> and <a href="/wiki/Grenade" title="Grenade">grenades</a> instead of rifles and issued <a href="/wiki/Camouflage" title="Camouflage">camouflage</a> clothing. He commanded the <a href="/wiki/5th_SS_Panzer_Division_Wiking" title="5th SS Panzer Division Wiking">SS Division <i>Wiking</i></a> and the <a href="/wiki/III_(Germanic)_SS_Panzer_Corps" title="III (Germanic) SS Panzer Corps">III (Germanic) SS Panzer Corps</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFlaherty2004147_23-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFlaherty2004147-23">[23]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Casualties">Casualties</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Waffen-SS&amp;action=edit&amp;section=44" title="Edit section: Casualties">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Military historian <a href="/wiki/R%C3%BCdiger_Overmans" title="Rüdiger Overmans">Rüdiger Overmans</a> estimates that the Waffen-SS suffered 314,000 dead.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-158"><a href="#cite_note-158">[155]</a></sup> Casualty rates were not significantly higher than in the Wehrmacht overall and were comparative to those among the <i>Heer</i> armoured divisions and the Luftwaffe paratroop formations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENeitzelWelzer2012300_159-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENeitzelWelzer2012300-159">[156]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Criminality">Criminality</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Waffen-SS&amp;action=edit&amp;section=45" title="Edit section: Criminality">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Stroop_Report_-_Warsaw_Ghetto_Uprising_06b.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1964" data-file-width="2766" height="156" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Stroop_Report_-_Warsaw_Ghetto_Uprising_06b.jpg/220px-Stroop_Report_-_Warsaw_Ghetto_Uprising_06b.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Stroop_Report_-_Warsaw_Ghetto_Uprising_06b.jpg/330px-Stroop_Report_-_Warsaw_Ghetto_Uprising_06b.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Stroop_Report_-_Warsaw_Ghetto_Uprising_06b.jpg/440px-Stroop_Report_-_Warsaw_Ghetto_Uprising_06b.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Stroop_Report_-_Warsaw_Ghetto_Uprising_06b.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Photograph from the <a href="/wiki/Stroop_Report" title="Stroop Report">Stroop Report</a>, prepared for <a href="/wiki/J%C3%BCrgen_Stroop" title="Jürgen Stroop">Jürgen Stroop</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <i><a href="/wiki/Allgemeine_SS" title="Allgemeine SS">Allgemeine SS</a></i> was responsible for the administration of both the <a href="/wiki/Nazi_concentration_camps" title="Nazi concentration camps">concentration</a> and <a href="/wiki/Extermination_camp" title="Extermination camp">extermination camps</a>. Many members of it and the <i><a href="/wiki/SS-Totenkopfverb%C3%A4nde" title="SS-Totenkopfverbände">SS-Totenkopfverbände</a></i> subsequently became members of the Waffen-SS, forming the initial core of the <a href="/wiki/3rd_SS_Panzer_Division_Totenkopf" title="3rd SS Panzer Division Totenkopf">3rd SS <i>Totenkopf</i> Division</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFlaherty2004149_29-8"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFlaherty2004149-29">[28]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFlaherty2004150_39-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFlaherty2004150-39">[38]</a></sup> A number of SS medical personnel who were members of the Waffen-SS were convicted of crimes during the "<a href="/wiki/Doctors%27_trial" title="Doctors' trial">Doctors' trials</a>" in Nuremberg, held between 1946 and 1947 for the <a href="/wiki/Nazi_human_experimentation" title="Nazi human experimentation">Nazi human experimentation</a> they performed at the camps.</p>
<p>According to the <i>Modern Genocide: The Definitive Resource and Document Collection</i>, the Waffen-SS had played a "paramount role" in the ideological war of extermination (<i>Vernichtungskrieg</i>), and not just as frontline or rear area security formations: a third of the <i><a href="/wiki/Einsatzgruppen" title="Einsatzgruppen">Einsatzgruppen</a></i> (mobile killing squads) members which were responsible for mass murder especially of Jews and communists, had been recruited from Waffen-SS personnel prior to the invasion of the Soviet Union.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBartropJacobs20141424_160-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBartropJacobs20141424-160">[157]</a></sup> Many Waffen-SS members and units were responsible for <a href="/wiki/War_crime" title="War crime">war crimes</a> against civilians and allied servicemen. After the war the SS organisation as a whole was held to be a criminal organization by the post-war German government. Formations such as the <i>Dirlewanger</i> and <a href="/wiki/29th_Waffen_Grenadier_Division_of_the_SS_RONA_(1st_Russian)" title="29th Waffen Grenadier Division of the SS RONA (1st Russian)">Kaminski Brigades</a> were singled out, and many others participated in large-scale massacres or smaller-scale killings such as murder of 34 captured allied servicemen ordered by <a href="/wiki/Josef_Kieffer" title="Josef Kieffer">Josef Kieffer</a> during <a href="/wiki/Operation_Bulbasket" title="Operation Bulbasket">Operation Bulbasket</a> in 1944, the Houtman affair,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEZimmermann2004_161-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEZimmermann2004-161">[158]</a></sup> or murders perpetrated by <a href="/wiki/Heinrich_Boere" title="Heinrich Boere">Heinrich Boere</a>. The listed Waffen-SS units were responsible for the following massacres:</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Car_in_Oradour-sur-Glane4.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1712" data-file-width="2288" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Car_in_Oradour-sur-Glane4.jpg/220px-Car_in_Oradour-sur-Glane4.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Car_in_Oradour-sur-Glane4.jpg/330px-Car_in_Oradour-sur-Glane4.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Car_in_Oradour-sur-Glane4.jpg/440px-Car_in_Oradour-sur-Glane4.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Car_in_Oradour-sur-Glane4.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Burned out cars and buildings still litter the remains of the original village in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Oradour-sur-Glane" title="Oradour-sur-Glane">Oradour-sur-Glane</a>, as left by Das Reich SS division</div>
</div>
</div>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Wormhoudt_massacre" title="Wormhoudt massacre">Wormhoudt massacre</a> by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/SS_Leibstandarte_Adolf_Hitler" title="SS Leibstandarte Adolf Hitler">SS Leibstandarte Adolf Hitler</a>, 1940, France<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWeale2012251.E2.80.93253_49-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWeale2012251.E2.80.93253-49">[48]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Le_Paradis_massacre" title="Le Paradis massacre">Le Paradis massacre</a> by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/SS_Division_Totenkopf" title="SS Division Totenkopf">SS Division Totenkopf</a>, 1940, France<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEStein198475.E2.80.9376_162-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEStein198475.E2.80.9376-162">[159]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Pripyat_swamps_(punitive_operation)" title="Pripyat swamps (punitive operation)">Pripyat swamps (punitive operation)</a> by the <a href="/wiki/SS_Cavalry_Brigade" title="SS Cavalry Brigade">SS Cavalry Brigade</a>, 1941, USSR<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMiller2006309.2C_310_163-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMiller2006309.2C_310-163">[160]</a></sup></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Oradour-sur-Glane" title="Oradour-sur-Glane">Oradour-sur-Glane massacre</a> by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/SS_Division_Das_Reich" title="SS Division Das Reich">SS Division Das Reich</a>, 1944, France</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ochota_massacre" title="Ochota massacre">Ochota massacre</a> by SS <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kaminski_Brigade" title="Kaminski Brigade">Kaminski Brigade</a>, 1944, Poland</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Wola_massacre" title="Wola massacre">Wola massacre</a> by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/SS-Sturmbrigade_Dirlewanger" title="SS-Sturmbrigade Dirlewanger">SS-Sturmbrigade Dirlewanger</a>, 1944, Poland</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Huta_Pieniacka_massacre" title="Huta Pieniacka massacre">Huta Pieniacka massacre</a> by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/14th_Waffen_Grenadier_Division_of_the_SS_Galizien_(1st_Ukrainian)" title="14th Waffen Grenadier Division of the SS Galizien (1st Ukrainian)">SS Division Galicia</a> 1944, Poland</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Tulle_massacre" title="Tulle massacre">Tulle massacre</a> by SS Division Das Reich, 1944, France</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Graignes" title="Battle of Graignes">Graignes Massacre</a> by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/SS_Division_G%C3%B6tz_von_Berlichingen" title="SS Division Götz von Berlichingen">SS Division Götz von Berlichingen</a>, 1944, France</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Maill%C3%A9_massacre" title="Maillé massacre">Maillé massacre</a>, also by SS Division Götz von Berlichingen, 1944, France</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Marzabotto_massacre" title="Marzabotto massacre">Marzabotto massacre</a> by <a href="/wiki/16th_SS_Panzergrenadier_Division_Reichsf%C3%BChrer-SS" title="16th SS Panzergrenadier Division Reichsführer-SS">16th SS Panzergrenadier Division Reichsführer-SS</a>, 1944, Italy</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Malmedy_massacre" title="Malmedy massacre">Malmedy massacre</a> by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kampfgruppe_Peiper" title="Kampfgruppe Peiper">Kampfgruppe Peiper</a>, part of 1st SS Panzer Division, 1944, Belgium</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ardeatine_massacre" title="Ardeatine massacre">Ardeatine massacre</a> by two SS officers, 1944, Italy</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Distomo_massacre" title="Distomo massacre">Distomo massacre</a> by 4th <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/SS_Polizei_Division" title="SS Polizei Division">SS Polizei Division</a>, 1944, Greece</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Sant%27Anna_di_Stazzema_massacre" title="Sant'Anna di Stazzema massacre">Sant'Anna di Stazzema massacre</a> by <a href="/wiki/16th_SS_Panzergrenadier_Division_Reichsf%C3%BChrer-SS" title="16th SS Panzergrenadier Division Reichsführer-SS">16th SS Panzergrenadier Division Reichsführer-SS</a>, 1944, Italy</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ardenne_Abbey_massacre" title="Ardenne Abbey massacre">Ardenne Abbey massacre</a> by <a href="/wiki/12th_SS_Panzer_Division_Hitlerjugend" title="12th SS Panzer Division Hitlerjugend">12th SS Panzer Division Hitlerjugend</a>, 1944, France</li>
</ul>
<p>The linking of the SS-VT with the <i>SS-Totenkopfverbände</i> (SS-TV) in 1938 raised important questions about Waffen-SS criminality,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFlaherty2004148_24-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFlaherty2004148-24">[24]</a></sup> since the SS-TV were already responsible for imprisonment, torture, and murder of Jews and other political opponents through providing the personnel for manning the concentration camps. Their leader, <a href="/wiki/Theodor_Eicke" title="Theodor Eicke">Theodor Eicke</a>, who was the commandant of Dachau, inspector of the camps, and murderer of <a href="/wiki/Ernst_R%C3%B6hm" title="Ernst Röhm">Ernst Röhm</a>, later became the commander of the 3rd SS <i>Totenkopf</i> Division.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFlaherty2004146_21-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFlaherty2004146-21">[21]</a></sup> With the invasion of Poland, the <i>Totenkopfverbände</i> troops were called on to carry out so-called "police and security measures" in rear areas. What these measures entailed is demonstrated by the record of <i>SS Totenkopf Standarte Brandenburg</i>. It arrived in <a href="/wiki/W%C5%82oc%C5%82awek" title="Włocławek">Włocławek</a> on 22 September 1939 and embarked on a four-day "Jewish action" that included the burning of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Synagogues" title="Synagogues">synagogues</a> and the execution en masse of the leaders of the Jewish community. On 29 September the Standarte travelled to <a href="/wiki/Bydgoszcz" title="Bydgoszcz">Bydgoszcz</a> to conduct an "intelligentsia action". Approximately 800 Polish civilians and what the <i><a href="/wiki/Sicherheitsdienst" title="Sicherheitsdienst">Sicherheitsdienst</a></i> (SD) termed "potential resistance leaders" were killed. Later the formation became the 3rd SS Panzer Division <i>Totenkopf</i>, but from the start they were among the first executors of a policy of systematic extermination.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:DeadBelgiumcivilians1944.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2030" data-file-width="2603" height="172" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/DeadBelgiumcivilians1944.jpg/220px-DeadBelgiumcivilians1944.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/DeadBelgiumcivilians1944.jpg/330px-DeadBelgiumcivilians1944.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/DeadBelgiumcivilians1944.jpg/440px-DeadBelgiumcivilians1944.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:DeadBelgiumcivilians1944.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Belgian civilians killed by German units during the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_the_Bulge" title="Battle of the Bulge">Battle of the Bulge</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Waffen-SS formations were found guilty of war crimes, especially in the opening and closing phases of the war.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEStein1984251_164-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEStein1984251-164">[161]</a></sup> In addition to documented atrocities, Waffen-SS units assisted in rounding up Eastern European Jews for deportation and utilised <a href="/wiki/Scorched_earth" title="Scorched earth">scorched earth</a> tactics during rear security operations. Some Waffen-SS personnel convalesced at concentration camps, from which they were drawn, by serving guard duties. Other members of the Waffen-SS were more directly involved in genocide.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWBSTV2007_165-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWBSTV2007-165">[162]</a></sup></p>
<p>The end of the war saw a number of war crime trials, including the <a href="/wiki/Malmedy_massacre_trial" title="Malmedy massacre trial">Malmedy massacre trial</a>. The counts of indictment related to the massacre of more than 300 American prisoners in the vicinity of <a href="/wiki/Malmedy" title="Malmedy">Malmedy</a>, between 16 December 1944 and 13 January 1945, and the massacre of 100 Belgian civilians mainly in the vicinity of <a href="/wiki/Stavelot" title="Stavelot">Stavelot</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEUS_War_Department1948_166-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEUS_War_Department1948-166">[163]</a></sup></p>
<p>During the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nuremberg_Trials" title="Nuremberg Trials">Nuremberg Trials</a>, the Waffen-SS was declared a criminal organisation,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEStein1984251_164-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEStein1984251-164">[161]</a></sup> except conscripts from 1943 onward, who were exempted from that judgement as they had been forced to join.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="HIAG">HIAG</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Waffen-SS&amp;action=edit&amp;section=46" title="Edit section: HIAG">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/HIAG" title="HIAG">HIAG</a></div>
<p><b>HIAG</b> (<a href="/wiki/German_language" title="German language">German</a>: <span lang="de" xml:lang="de"><i><b>Hi</b>lfsgemeinschaft <b>a</b>uf <b>G</b>egenseitigkeit der Angehörigen der ehemaligen Waffen-SS</i></span>, literally "Mutual aid association of former Waffen-SS members") was a <a href="/wiki/Advocacy_group" title="Advocacy group">lobby group</a> and a revisionist veterans' organisation founded by former high-ranking Waffen-SS personnel in <a href="/wiki/West_Germany" title="West Germany">West Germany</a> in 1951. It campaigned for the legal, economic and historical rehabilitation of the Waffen-SS, using contacts with political parties to manipulate them for its purposes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELarge1987_167-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELarge1987-167">[164]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDer_Spiegel2011_168-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDer_Spiegel2011-168">[165]</a></sup></p>
<p>HIAG's <a href="/wiki/Historical_revisionism" title="Historical revisionism">historical revisionism</a> encompassed multi-prong <a href="/wiki/Propaganda" title="Propaganda">propaganda efforts</a>, including periodicals, books and public speeches, alongside a publishing house that served as a platform for its publicity aims.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMacKenzie1997135.E2.80.93141_169-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMacKenzie1997135.E2.80.93141-169">[166]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWilke2011398.E2.80.93399_170-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWilke2011398.E2.80.93399-170">[167]</a></sup> This extensive body of work – 57 book titles and more than 50 years of monthly periodicals – have been described by historians as revisionist <a href="/wiki/Apologia" title="Apologia">apologia</a>: [a] "chorus of self-justification";<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMacKenzie1997137_171-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMacKenzie1997137-171">[168]</a></sup> "crucible of historical revisionism";<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPicaper2014_172-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPicaper2014-172">[169]</a></sup> "false" and "outrageous" claims;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDiehl1993225_173-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDiehl1993225-173">[170]</a></sup> "most important works of [Waffen-SS] apologist literature" (in reference to books by Hausser and Steiner);<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESydnor1990319_174-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESydnor1990319-174">[171]</a></sup> and "exculpating multi-volume chronicle" (in reference to the history of the SS Division <i>Leibstandarte</i>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEParker2014217_175-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEParker2014217-175">[172]</a></sup></p>
<p>Given the connection with its Nazi past, HIAG was a subject of significant controversy, both in West Germany and abroad.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELarge1987_167-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELarge1987-167">[164]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDer_Spiegel2011_168-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDer_Spiegel2011-168">[165]</a></sup> The organisation moved into <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Right-wing_extremism" title="Right-wing extremism">right-wing extremism</a> in its later history. It was disbanded in 1992 at the federal level, but local groups, along with the organisation's monthly periodical, continued to exist at least into the 2000s.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWertherHurd2014_176-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWertherHurd2014-176">[173]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELevenda2014167_177-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELevenda2014167-177">[174]</a></sup></p>
<p>While the HIAG leadership only partially achieved the goals of legal and economic rehabilitation of Waffen-SS,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDiehl1993236_178-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDiehl1993236-178">[175]</a></sup> falling short of their "extravagant fantasies about [Waffen-SS's] past and future",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELarge1987111.E2.80.93112_179-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELarge1987111.E2.80.93112-179">[176]</a></sup> HIAG's propaganda efforts have led to a reshaping of the image of <a href="/wiki/Waffen-SS_in_popular_culture" title="Waffen-SS in popular culture">Waffen-SS in popular culture</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMacKenzie1997135.E2.80.93141_169-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMacKenzie1997135.E2.80.93141-169">[166]</a></sup> The results are still felt, with scholarly treatments being drowned out by a "veritable avalanche of titles",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWegner19901_180-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWegner19901-180">[177]</a></sup> including amateur historical studies, memoirs, picture books, websites, and wargames.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESmelserDavies2008135_181-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESmelserDavies2008135-181">[178]</a></sup></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Explanatory_notes">Explanatory notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Waffen-SS&amp;action=edit&amp;section=48" title="Edit section: Explanatory notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: lower-alpha;">
<ol class="references">
<li id="cite_note-27"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-27">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Equivalent to a full General. The independence of the LSSAH can be partly explained by Dietrich's rank, as well as his personal friendship with Hitler.</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-117"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-117">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">"Adolf Hitler is not interested in further existence of Warsaw ... the whole population shall be executed and all buildings blown up." <a href="#CITEREFMadajczyk1972">Madajczyk 1972</a>, p. 390.</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-118"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-118">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">According to the evidence of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Erich_von_dem_Bach" title="Erich von dem Bach">Erich von dem Bach</a> in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/International_Military_Tribunal" title="International Military Tribunal">Nürnberg</a>, Himmler's order (issued on the strength of an order of Hitler), read as follows: "1. Caught razed insurgents shall be killed despite whether they fight in accordance with the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hague_Conventions_(1899_and_1907)" title="Hague Conventions (1899 and 1907)">Hague Convention</a> or they infringe it. 2. Non-fighting part of population, women, children, shall also be killed. 3. All the city shall be razed to the ground, i.e. buildings, streets, facilities in that city, and everything which is within its borders." <a href="#CITEREFWroniszewski1970">Wroniszewski 1970</a>, pp. 128–129.</span></li>
</ol>

<li><cite class="citation journal" id="CITEREFZwack1999">Zwack, Peter (1999). <a class="external text" href="http://www.historynet.com/world-war-ii-siege-of-budapest.htm/14" rel="nofollow">"World War II: Siege of Budapest"</a>. <i>Quarterly Journal of Military History</i>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AWaffen-SS&amp;rft.atitle=World+War+II%3A+Siege+of+Budapest&amp;rft.aufirst=Peter&amp;rft.aulast=Zwack&amp;rft.date=1999&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.historynet.com%2Fworld-war-ii-siege-of-budapest.htm%2F14&amp;rft.jtitle=Quarterly+Journal+of+Military+History&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal"><span style="display:none;"> </span></span></li>
